Where did all that tension from before go?

His switch between formality and informality was too drastic.

“Excuse me for interrupting your conversation. Your rooms have been prepared, so I have come to escort you, adventurers.”

This was a lifesaver. To avoid Wilhelm’s strangely aggressive pursuit, we decided to fully accept the Attendant’s offer to guide us. However, a Knight stopped Alex, who was about to walk out with us.

“We have prepared a separate room for Alex-sama. Another person will escort you later, so please wait here for a moment.”

“…Understood. Zarumen, I’m counting on you over there.”

“Got it.”

Alex seemed reluctant but obediently complied.

This was likely another result of the Old Knight’s conversation just now. It was like we were being starkly confronted with the difference in status that had always existed between him and us, but which had been completely invisible until now.

“I’ll come visit later, so make sure you wait for me, okay?”

I wondered if the gap between us would continue to widen.

The next moment, those words slipped out of my mouth.

It might be inappropriate to talk about playing when we came here to work. As proof, some of the Knights shot me sharp glances. They seemed to be telling me to know my place. I was sure my impression had worsened. Even so—

“Yeah, I’ll be waiting.”

The moment I saw Alex’s relieved face, I forgot all about regret.

I couldn’t leave him alone, not after he’d called me a precious comrade.

I absolutely didn’t want to let go of the hand he’d extended to me.

I thought my emotions were rather youthful. Including my past life, I should be over 50, but I couldn’t see any vision of myself becoming a dignified and flexible handsome older man like Wilhelm.

Was my thinking being pulled back by my physical age? Or had my spirit not grown at all since then? On the way to the room that had been prepared for us, I kept asking myself those very questions.

+++

# **66 - Shared Feelings**

The room assigned to us was the building that the adventurers had originally used as their base. The interior and layout seemed largely unchanged, but the room had been meticulously cleaned, and broken shelves and furniture appeared to have been repaired. The moldy sheets on the well-worn beds had been replaced with brand-new cloth, a significant upgrade.

It was definitely cleaner than the cheap lodgings in the Slums. It was almost a pity that we wouldn’t be able to stay here for long, as we planned to enter the Dungeon starting tomorrow.

“I’m thinking of going to Alex’s place. Want to come along?”

It was a little past noon. Since we had some time to kill until dinner, I decided to visit Alex as I had promised earlier. I invited Zash, Mikkusu, and Buriddo, who were sharing the room. I thought that chatting with Alex would be a good way to deepen my relationship with them, as we weren’t very close.

“I think I’ll pass. I’ll just clean my tools here.”

“I’m really seasick from the carriage ride. Let me rest here for tomorrow.”

“…I’m feeling a bit off, too… Sorry…”

The replies from the three of them were unenthusiastic. Their complexions weren’t very good either.

Though they didn’t explicitly say it, their attitude was one of rejection.

I figured I shouldn’t force them and backed off immediately.

We adventurers were at the bottom of society. The difference in status, the difference in the worlds we lived in, the fact that they had a place to return to… The sight we were just shown must have been shocking to them. Especially since Alex also possessed the skill of an adventurer. They seemed to be severely shaken mentally. The gap that had formed between Alex and them must be more serious than I imagined.

“I see. Well, I’m heading out then.”

Jealousy and envy toward successful adventurers weren’t uncommon. They could even cause a Party to break up. In fact, I’d seen many parties like that. A similar atmosphere was hanging around them.

“I hope it doesn’t affect our activities in the Dungeon.”

I muttered to myself after leaving the room.

I was worried, but it wasn’t something I could fix. I was a veteran adventurer, technically. But I lacked the dignity and the skill. No matter how many words I used to persuade or encourage them, it probably wouldn’t resonate. I stopped thinking about it.

---

Guided by a Knight, I visited Alex’s room.

It seemed to be a renovated room in the back of the Church. A thick, long-piled Carpet was laid on the floor, and a Tapestry depicting a Goddess seated on a Scale was hung on the wall. It was clear at a glance that this room was prepared for a person of special status.

His figure, seated on a massive Chair in the center of the room, was like that of a subject in a painting. He rested his cheek on his hand, crossed his legs, and idly played with his flowing red hair while giving me a languid gaze. His attitude looked bad, but the fact that he completely pulled off the pose made me envious of handsome guys.

“Yo, I came as promised.”

“Only you…?”

“What is it? Are you disappointed it’s just me?”

“No, it’s as I expected. Though I find it vexing.”

The aura of ill-humor that had surrounded him instantly vanished.

What was that? How does he turn it on and off?

“That damn Old Man! He’s always testing my friends!”

“Ah, so he was testing us.”

“Of course! He tries to justify it by saying he needs to see if they’re Vermin trying to cling to the Marquis’s family power… Thanks to him, I don’t have many friends among the Nobles either! How much I resented him for it when I was a child!”

He pounded the armrest, openly expressing his anger.

It felt unusual for him to vent his emotions so directly.

“…Wilhelm was my tutor. When I was a child, I even thought he was my real father… So, well, you know… Don’t look at me with that smirk!”

“You were happy to see him again after all this time, right?”

“…Well, yes.”

Alex crossed his arms and let out a rough ‘Hmph.’

He softened his expression, looking pleased despite his bright red cheeks.

“Zash and the others were confused. They must have felt the difference in status more than they expected. I think they’ll want to keep their distance for a while. In that sense, it might be good that we’ll be operating separately for a bit starting tomorrow.”

“…What about Marī and the others?”

“They looked better than Zash and the others. Since the men and women are in separate rooms, I haven’t been able to talk to them, but I think they’re fine.”

“…I see… I hope so…”

I gave a stern word to the weakly smiling Alex.

“Hey, hey, aren’t you being too girly today!? Where’s your usual arrogant and defiant attitude!? Alex is the one who laughs fearlessly and kicks trouble to the curb, right!? Pull yourself together!”

“H-Huh!? What do you take me for!? Is it so wrong to feel down sometimes!? I get to feel sentimental sometimes too! Do you have no Delicacy!?”

“I don’t need Delicacy for you! Besides, that sentimental attitude doesn’t suit you!”

“…What, Huh, HAAAAH!?”

Alex, who could only open and close his mouth and tremble with teary eyes, had completely lost his vocabulary. He looked like he was about to cry, desperately trying to hold back the tears.

Seriously, Alex was acting totally unlike himself today.

“My Alex isn’t the kind of guy who gets nervous just because some commoners are put off! He’s always confident and cool! That’s what I like about you!”

“HAAAAAAH!?”

I felt like I was speaking out of desperation.

I didn’t even know what I was saying anymore.

Maybe I was also telling this to myself.

“You’re the one who dragged everyone into this Dungeon raid! You’re the one who started this, wanting to save Marī and our comrades! We don’t know if the Magic Tool that can truly save her exists. But we are here because we believe in Alex!”

I wanted to believe.

In the power I’ve acquired.

In the comrades who motivated me.

“We are comrades who respect you and followed you.”

I grabbed Alex’s shoulder and faced him directly.

My reflection was visible in his wavering eyes.

I was speaking to myself through Alex.

“Believe. The bonds we forged facing life and death aren’t that fragile.”

I settled my feelings about that incident at the Guild.

The comrades I believed in wouldn’t betray me.

I wanted to believe that. So I would believe.

“…! Let go of me… Your fingers hurt a little…”

“Eh, ah, sorry!”

Unbeknownst to me, I had apparently squeezed too hard.

Perhaps because I was too emotional, I couldn’t control my strength properly.

“Don’t worry about it; your feelings came across painfully well. …So, I don’t feel bad about it at all.”

Alex, leaning back deeply in the Chair, let out a deep breath. Alex covered his eyes with the back of his right hand. I couldn’t see what expression he was making.

I regretted letting my emotions run wild.

His anxiety and my anxiety were of the same kind. That’s why I had inadvertently projected myself onto Alex. His uncharacteristically weak attitude might have felt like a reflection of my own heart.

How pathetic.

I thought I had completely mastered the art of controlling my emotions when I was working as an adult in my previous life. Recently, I felt myself becoming easily swayed by impulses born from emotion. I should be able to handle myself better. How utterly pathetic.

“Hey.”

Alex asked me a question.

His face was still hidden, but his voice was much calmer.

“You said you liked me, right?”

“…Yeah, I did. I certainly did. It just burst out in the heat of the moment…”

Looking back, I was burning with shame.

It was the first time I’d ever said I liked a man.

I could barely say I liked someone even to a woman.

“It’s not… in a sexual way, is it?”

“Of course not! I’m Normal!”

“…Then, that’s fine… I’m relieved…”

“By ‘like,’ I mean, well, it’s… respect. I looked up to Alex’s success as an adventurer. You quickly gained skill and passed me, even reaching Silver Rank… I felt frustrated, envious, and jealous… I wanted to hate you, but I couldn’t.”

I was confessing my honest feelings to Alex for the first time.

“You’re a First-Magnitude Star shining far away in the night sky, completely out of reach. But whenever I look up, you’re always flashing brightly somewhere. That’s the man Alex who I like.”

“I’ve been thinking this for a while, but where did you, a commoner, learn such affected lines?”

“Hmm, ah, it’s probably that. I might have remembered something a Bard was singing that sounded like that from the corner of my memory.”

“Seriously, weren’t you a Noble somewhere?”

“That’s not it. I’m a Bastard born in a Brothel in the Slums, you know? Noble status doesn’t suit me.”

“I see. I have mixed feelings of happiness and sadness hearing that you weren’t born a Noble. It’s a strange feeling.”

“Yeah, that certainly is a strange thing to say.”

I vaguely pondered what Alex had said.

What would have happened if I had been born a Noble in this world? Would I have been like, ‘Reincarnated Noble, Harem Hooray!’ or ‘Knowledge Cheat, Hooray!’? …I suppose, in that case, Alex and I would have been fated never to meet. That feels a little lonely.

“Hey, Zarumen.”

“What is it?”

“I want you to stay by my side forever.”

“…I told you, I’m Normal…”

“It would be troublesome for me if you weren’t. I just said so, didn’t I?”

Alex chuckled softly, finding something amusing.

“That was the first time. The first time I’ve been admonished so forcefully. Neither my Father nor Wilhelm has ever thrown words at me so strongly. The warmth that transferred from your fingertips strongly resonated in my heart, and it was so comforting.”

He slowly lowered his arm.

His red, tear-swollen eyes were redder than usual.

“It seems… I like you too.”

He looked at me with those moist eyes and spoke those words.

My heart gave a huge jump. I wanted to believe that him looking oddly sexy was just my imagination.

“We’re Mutually in Love, Zarumen.”

“Stop it, stop it! Ugh, that’s gross!”

“Pff, chuckle… Hahahaha! Well, well, you certainly make a good sound!”

“Okay, okay! I’m glad your mood has recovered enough to tease me like that! Ugh, I’m getting shivers!”

Alex laughed heartily.

He must have completely sorted out his feelings. He had a cheerful expression. That was good, but I couldn’t understand why he could smile so refreshingly while I was getting goosebumps.

“…Being able to confide our feelings without reserve. Being able to talk from the heart. That’s the friend I’ve always wanted…”

He whispered the words softly.

I couldn’t hear the content, but seeing his happy smile, I couldn’t tease him anymore. I thought once again how lucky handsome people are.

However, I secretly thanked him in my heart.

The sediment that had been building up in my chest since the incident at the Guild had been completely swept away by our interaction. I decided to trust my comrades. I decided to trust myself. I spoke and let out all the vague anxiety about possibly being betrayed by my comrades again. All that remained in my empty chest was a burning resolve.

“Alex, we’re going to succeed in this adventure together, no matter what!”

“…! Yes, we’ll definitely accomplish it together!”

We knocked our fists together in a hard clash.

In his gleaming eyes, I could clearly see myself, my eyes gleaming just the same.

+++

# **67 - Dungeon Attack! (1)**

The underground Marra Dungeon, which I visited again after a month, was filled with the same Stillness as before.

The air was clear and untainted. There was no smell of dust.

The Dungeon had a peculiar atmosphere, giving a sense of unexpected crispness for an underground space.

If I hadn’t encountered that dreadful monster, the sanctity-like feeling of the air here might have completely shattered all my vigilance. It was that potent.

“Cindy, is everything okay on your side?”

“No problems.”

We were the first to descend, just the two of us, ahead of the other members.

It was the Scout’s job to check if the destination was safe.

Apparently, some Dungeons were the “living” type, where the layout of traps and passages changed every time you enter. Fortunately, I hadn’t yet stepped into such a troublesome Dungeon, but ever since I heard about it, I’ve been extra vigilant in Dungeons. It’s not uncommon for fellow adventurers or Thief Guilds using the Dungeon as a lair to set new traps.

There shouldn’t have been any new intruders since the Knights secured the base, but it was better to be safe than sorry. The check came up empty this time, which was a relief. I lightly sighed in relief.

“—It’s safe! Come on down!”

I shouted.

After a while, the loud clomp, clomp of Military Boots descending broke the silence of the place. They descended into the Dungeon in this order: several Knights at the front, followed by Alex and his party, and finally, another unit of Knights.

The First Assault Team totaled 518 people.

We were 8 adventurers, 10 Knights, and their Squires and Attendants made up the remaining 500. This was a tiny number compared to the entire force gathered at the base, but it was far too many people to gather inside a Dungeon.

“Form ranks!”

The Knights immediately formed their ranks at a single command. It was magnificent.

“The Assault Team shall follow Alex-sama’s Adventurer Party and proceed east, toward the deeper levels of the Dungeon! The Search Team must first secure the safety of this surrounding area, and then establish a Supply Route to the Assault Team! Begin operation!”

“Yes, sir!”

The adventurers were overwhelmed by the impressive Proficiency and Military Presence of the Army.

Zash and the others, in particular, looked intimidated.

Ultimately, the three of them had continued to maintain their distance from Alex since the incident yesterday.

Alex didn’t seem to mind much.

He also didn’t seem to be trying to close the distance himself.

He was much quieter than usual, but his complexion was good.

Since he seemed to be full of confidence and power, there was probably no need to worry.

“Zash, Mikkusu, Buriddo. Don’t be so nervous. We adventurers are the veterans in the Dungeon, you know? You should act as if you’re dealing with a Newcomer adventurer.”

“…Yeah, you’re right. I’ll try to manage somehow. We’ve been adventurers for a long time, too, not as long as you, but still. We can’t let a bunch of rookies look down on us!”

“Heheh, how pathetic… I was so jumpy it was like we were the Newcomers again… Sorry, I made you worry.”

“I-I’ll do my best!”

Their expressions were still stiff, but they seemed to have regained some vitality.

With this, they probably wouldn’t make any careless mistakes.

“Alright, let’s go, too. Cindy, take the lead.”

“Aye!”

“W-Wait for us!”

A voice called out to my back as I was about to leave the spot.

“You guys be careful, too, Alex!”

“Yeah, you’ve got the more dangerous job!”

“D-Do your best, Alex!”

The three of them called out to us—no, to Alex.

They seemed very nervous, but they were looking straight at him.

Alex was caught off guard, his eyes widening.

“Thank you.”

However, he immediately broke his expression and replied with a soft smile. The man who had worn that downcast expression was nowhere to be seen. His current demeanor was full of composure and confidence.

“You three don’t let your guard down, either.”

A sudden gust of wind gently lifted his long hair, making him look like a Lion elegantly shaking its tail. This time, it was the three of them who widened their eyes. They stared blankly, mesmerized by Alex.

“…Hmph! Looks like I worried for nothing!”

“Everything just looks too cool on him. It’s almost embarrassing for us…”

“…He’s so Cool…”

I wanted to believe that the faint blush on their cheeks was an optical illusion.

The gap that had formed between them also seemed to have closed. I think the worst crisis, the potential collapse of the Party, had passed. That was a very good thing. …But, somehow, I wasn’t entirely satisfied.

“Handsome guys really get away with too much…”

I muttered under my breath so no one could hear.

My small envy dissolved smoothly into the Dungeon’s darkness.

---

We proceeded east through the Dungeon.

Cindy and I were leading the Assault Team.

“Zaryū, they’re there.”

“Which way?”

“Right.”

“How many?”

“Three Golems.”

Upon receiving Cindy’s report, I signaled the members behind me. The Knights who were on standby immediately formed ranks and launched a preemptive attack on the Golems. Two Knights, leading a squad, attacked each Golem.

The underground Marra Dungeon had high ceilings and wide passages, making it an easy environment where adventurers’ movements weren’t restricted. However, it seemed that wasn’t the case for the Knights. Their basic tactic seemed to be operating their subordinate Soldiers in units of a dozen or so, and applying that as-is was too restrictive for an underground environment.

Therefore, we had them reorganize their squads into smaller units and actively engage in combat to get used to the Dungeon environment. The plan was originally for the Knights to primarily handle the combat that occurred inside the Dungeon, so the situation hadn’t changed. If there was a miscalculation, it was this:

“They’re slow.”

Marī’s quiet voice sharply pierced through the clamor of the battle.

This was already the third battle inside the Dungeon, but from the perspective of us adventurers, the Knights seemed to be taking an oddly long time for each fight.

Adventurers preferred to finish a battle quickly.

You never knew when you’d be attacked, whether in a Dungeon or the Wilderness. Since you always had to be ready for the next fight, you wrapped up combat as soon as possible. If it dragged on too long, you didn’t insist on a conclusion; you ran away quickly and regrouped.

If your baggage or equipment was in the way, you threw it all away and fled naked.

You couldn’t live long without that kind of mindset.

It wasn’t that their movements were poor. Following the Knight’s commands, they steadily chipped away at and cornered the enemy with excellent coordination. In fact, their combat power and proficiency were visibly high. They were thoroughly equipped with the military strength needed to survive in this world of endless warfare. They didn’t seem to lack practical combat experience either.

The simplest explanation was probably a large difference in Level.

In this world with Levels, an individual’s strength wasn’t determined by appearance.

A muscular, bearded Warrior struck the Golem’s knee with a full-power hammer blow, unbalancing it. It was a truly magnificent blow… but if Clair had struck the same spot with a full-power blow, she could have completely shattered the Golem’s knee, preventing it from ever standing up again. Since even the seemingly delicate Clair could do that with Level 11, we could assume the Soldiers led by the Knights had even lower Levels.

“Well, it’s better than rushing and taking casualties. We’re a little behind schedule, but it’s only the first day. This isn’t the time to panic. Right, Zarumen?”

Alex sought my opinion in a clear tone.

This was a deliberate show, meant for the Knights and Soldiers waiting nearby.

I caught his drift and answered with a loud voice.

“Combat in the Dungeon is dangerous if you’re not used to it. I think it’s a good idea to get used to the environment now. This experience should be helpful for what’s to come.”

“…What do you mean by that?”

One of the Knights couldn’t help but step forward and ask me.

His Visor was down, so I couldn’t see his expression, but he had a dignified aura. Was he a Young Knight? He was a bit short, only coming up to my shoulder, but his chest-out, confident stance looked genuinely cool.

“It sounds like you are dissatisfied with our Knights’ fighting style. Are you worried about the existence of that monster you mentioned? Or are you suggesting that our skills, the skill of the Libra Marquis’s Knights, are inferior to you, an adventurer?”

He pressed me with his words, tinged with slight indignation. Apparently, he thought I was an adventurer disrespecting a Knight. Or perhaps it was jealousy that a dubious man of unknown origin was being asked for his opinion by Alex.

“Bernkatze, he—”

“Young Master, I am asking this adventurer for his true intentions! Since the Young Master himself declared that he is an adventurer here, please keep silent for now!”

A sharp glare, visible through the gaps in his Visor, fixed on Alex.

“Now, Adventurer, answer me!”

The Knight, called Bernkatze, roared, spouting heated breath. The surrounding Knights made no move to stop him. This implicitly suggested they supported his claim.

I glanced at Alex, and he gave a small nod. His lips moved: “I leave it to you.”

No, no, no. Don’t just dump the problem on me—but since the opponent had me firmly locked on, I probably couldn’t escape. I felt a sigh about to escape.

“…Honestly, I think you’re Underleveled.”

“What!? Are you insulting us Knights!?”

“I didn’t intend to insult you. I just stated a fact.”

The Knights’ gazes sharpened at my statement.

“Adventurers use the time spent in combat as a measure of strength. If a fight drags on, there’s a risk of other enemies jumping in. Not fighting an opponent you can’t defeat easily is the trick to a long life for adventurers. From our perspective as adventurers, it seems you’re taking far too long to defeat them.”

“…! So you’re saying our fighting style is wrong…”

“That’s how it is.”

In contrast to my calm reply, the Knights tightly clenched their fists.

“…Phew, I understand. We should focus on the time it takes for a subjugation, correct? Specifically, what is the ideal time to finish a single battle?”

“Around three minutes.”

“Alright, we’ll aim for that next time. …I’ll overlook the matter of the insult.”

Bernkatze stomped his Military Boots against the Dungeon floor and returned to the other Knights. The way they immediately began exchanging opinions had a chilling intensity.

“Sorry. Bernkatze isn’t a bad guy, but… he has a very rigid personality. We often fought when we were kids.”

“Haha, I can tell…”

The free-spirited Alex, born a Noble but becoming an adventurer, and Bernkatze, who seemed like the embodiment of Noble Pride, probably didn’t get along.

“But I’m glad he seems to like you.”

“…Me, like him?”

“Hahaha, the reverse! Bernkatze is just awkward.”

What part of that conversation suggested he liked me?

If anything, he was still glaring at me now and then! His gaze was so sharp it was scary.

Somehow, that sharpness reminded me of Wilhelm, the Knight Commander.

“…Besides, don’t cling to me so much! I’m already being glared at by the Knights because of that exchange, and if you stay this close, I’m worried it’ll just make the Knights even angrier!”

“That’s wrong! It’s the opposite! I’m emphasizing our closeness and letting everyone know that you’re my favorite! In other words, I’m sticking to you for your own safety! Come on, you understand how I feel, don’t you…”

“Aargh, stop making that creepy voice right next to my ear!”

It seemed Alex’s sense of personal space had broken since yesterday’s incident.

I could feel goosebumps rising on my spine as he whispered to me in a wheedling voice.

The fierce battle with the Golems was still ongoing behind me, and an ominous Killing Intent was being directed at me from Bernkatze ahead. And,

“He really might have developed a strange hobby…”

Marī’s quietly muttered voice slipped into my ear. It wasn’t just Marī; Clair and Cindy were also giving me looks of suspicion.

“We’re in a Dungeon! Give me a break already!”

I was learning the trivial fact that Adventurers with too much time on their hands never do anything good.

+++

# **68 - Dungeon Attack! (2)**

The air circulating in the Dungeon changed.

It was an unpleasant air, heavy with a sticky, clinging discomfort that wrapped around the skin.

I could also sense a faint, rotten odor mixed in. With every step forward, the sensation of my skin prickling intensified, and the smell became clearly distinguishable.

I could hear the agitated whispers of the Knights following behind.

They must have also noticed that something unusual was rapidly approaching.

A sense of tension propagated throughout the entire group.

“Zaryū, can you hear it?”

“…The sound of water, I think.”

“It’s flowing. Maybe a Garden.”

Cindy’s voice was rigid and strained.

If there was a Garden ahead, it would be a situation extremely similar to when we encountered the Aberrant Monsters. That terrible calamity, which befell us because we had been complacent, believing we were safe due to the Sanctuary’s Magic, must have deeply wounded both Cindy’s body and mind.

“I’ll go take a look first.”

“No, Cindy goes.”

Cindy stiffened her expression but proudly puffed out her chest, pushing me aside and stepping forward.

“Cindy is more agile. Zaryū must protect the Baggage.”

Cindy sharply scolded me, whose emotions had gotten ahead of me.

It was a foolish remark, knowing the potential danger ahead. If we lost the Baggage here, it would be difficult to continue the exploration. That would defeat the purpose.

“…You’re right. Sorry, I’ll leave it to Cindy.”

She was more composed than I was.

I pulled myself together and focused my mind.

“Take this with you.”

I took an item out of my Pouch and handed it to her.

A Spirit Stone. It was a Magic Tool created by processing a Magic Stone. Its mechanism involved the sealed Magic Power within being released and diffused upon a strong impact, generating an intense flash, shockwave, and sound for an instant, which served to stun the target it hit.

In short, it was a Magical Flashbang.

It was effective even against Monsters without a physical form, so I figured it would work on those Aberrant Monsters. Even if it didn’t stun them, the loud blast and flash would let our comrades know that there was trouble.

It wasn’t a particularly expensive item, but the quantity we could obtain was limited. For the relatively weak me, it was a vital item, a lifesaver to keep for emergencies, but I didn’t hesitate to give it to Cindy.

“Thanks.”

Cindy flashed a quick grin and ran into the depths of the Dungeon as I watched her go.

A moment of silence.

Clang! A sound of something hard shattering into pieces echoed from the distance.

Shortly after, a flash of light and a roar.

A dreadful, scratching shriek rose from the Dungeon’s darkness.

“Alex!”

“Those things showed up, didn’t they!? Watch out, the Black Monsters are coming!”

“Tch! All units, intercept position! Form up!”

Roars and shouts flew back and forth, and Military Boots scrambled around.

The Knights were visibly agitated but instantly prepared their stance for battle.

Alex and the others also ran to my side, ready for combat.

I didn’t spare them a glance, aiming my favorite Crossbow and staring fixedly into the darkness.

A few seconds, or perhaps ten seconds. It appeared before the sweat running down my cheek could hit the ground.

“——————!!”

A monster of hideous design, as if formed by lumps of melted, black human figures.

Piercing shrieks were unleashed from its countless mouths. Its vacant eyes didn’t reflect anything, yet I felt them staring directly at us living beings.

The creatures oozed black Tar and crawled out of the darkness, closing in.

I pulled the trigger without hesitation.

“——————!!”

The monster let out a bloodcurdling, dreadful scream. Without flinching, I fired the next shot. The Repeating Crossbow ceaselessly spat out bolts. By the time I emptied the magazine, the leading figure had completely stopped moving.

However, there was no time for relief.

Monsters continued to pour out one after another from behind the fallen one.

Five bodies, ten bodies… they swarmed out of the Dungeon’s depths.

“Don’t falter! Attack!”

The Knights clashed head-on with the monsters. Their tactic was to have the Shields absorb the enemy’s blow and use a counter-attack from the Strikers to finish them off. Having grasped the fundamentals in the fight with the Golems, they seemed to be performing their roles admirably, but.

“Guaaah!”

“Damn it, this black sludge… Guooohh!”

“My skin, my skin is burning! It hurts!”

The black liquid, whether spat out from the monster’s mouth or spilled from wounds inflicted by attacks, was a terrifying attack against humans.

“Wash off any black bodily fluids with Holy Water! Be careful not to let it touch your skin directly!”

Bernkatze shouted commands.

The Knights had apparently prepared measures against the Curse Attacks. Some Knights appeared to have the fluid hit something and dissipate, as if they were wrapped in a thin membrane, just before the black spray of the monster’s blood could touch them. Perhaps strong Blessed Armor, Amulets, or Magic to defend against such attacks could nullify it.

“Take this!”

“‘23 Bolts’ ‘Deploy’ ‘Magic Arrow’!”

Alex, his sword wreathed in roaring flames, cut down a cluster of monsters in a single sweep. The monsters that were about to pounce on Alex, who had exposed himself by unleashing a full-power strike, were all instantly pierced and incapacitated by Marī’s unleashed Magic Arrows. I almost found myself mesmerized by the sight of the two of them in action.

The scene was already a chaotic melee. The Knights seemed to have been divided into several groups and couldn’t maximize their advantage in numbers because they had to deal with the monsters individually. Since our Adventurer Group was at the forefront of the Assault Team, we were isolated from the Knights’ main force. Prioritizing our safety, this would be the moment to rejoin the Knights.

But—even though the monsters had attacked us, Cindy, who should have used the Spirit Stone and fled, hadn’t reached us yet. It wasn’t that I missed her in the sudden chaos. Had she failed to escape, or had the monsters blocked her retreat? In any case, Cindy was still ahead.

“Everyone, follow me! We’re going to go get Cindy!”

I completed the magazine exchange and called out to my comrades.

“I will clear the way. You decide the direction.”

“Leave the rear to me.”

“I’ll keep watch while we move!”

Everyone answered without a second thought.

With that, Alex dashed toward the depths of the Dungeon without hesitation, and Marī and Clair encouraged me with powerful words. I had no doubt. I ran as fast as I could, side-by-side with them.

We advanced through the Dungeon, sweeping the monsters aside.

Both the right and left were overflowing with Aberrant Monsters.

If we hesitated, we would be surrounded instantly.

Clutching my Crossbow, ready to use at any moment, I desperately ran through the path Alex and Marī carved open.

A popping sound echoed in the distance. A faint flash of light caught the edge of my vision.

That must have been the Spirit Stone I gave Cindy.

“That way! We’re cutting straight through the Garden!”

Two more flashes and roars in quick succession.

The Spirit Stones I gave Cindy must have all been used up with that.

“Cindy, this way! I’m coming for you!”

The noise from the fighting was too loud to hear anything clearly, but I still felt as if someone had answered my shout.

A monster, slain by someone other than us, lay dead. Just beyond it, I saw a small crouching shadow and an excited, rearing monster. Vicious, sticky Tar dripped from the monster’s unnaturally vertical, torn jaw like saliva, stringing black threads.

Alex dashed at full speed, but he wouldn’t make it in time. Marī was behind me, so the monster would be out of her sight from her position. Her Magic Arrows were difficult to hit with if the target wasn’t in her line of sight. Next to me, Clair let out a silent scream.

“Don’t you dare lay a hand on her!”

I aimed my Crossbow on the spot and desperately pulled the trigger. The bolts were drawn in and all hit, but they weren’t enough to kill the monster. The distance had made the power insufficient. Its movements slowed, but the monster was still alive.

The next time I blinked,

That grotesquely torn jaw might be devouring something.

Was my only option to pray that Alex would arrive in time?

—Even though I gained power. Could I not accomplish anything?

“…! Take this!”

I drew the sword hanging at my waist with all my might.

I threw it with all my strength toward the enemy. It was a desperate act. The sword, a heavy object, should naturally lose momentum and fall to the ground—but it didn’t. It suddenly accelerated, flying through the air horizontally.

Boom! A sound of flesh exploding echoed.

The sword, thrust into the center of the monster, carved a large Crater into its aberrant body.

The sword stuck in the monster glowed faintly, but the light quickly subsided.

The monster’s shadow shriveled with a splash of dirty water.

“…Did I just do that?”

The words slipped out.

I was momentarily stunned by the unexpected result and the sight before me.

“Zaryū! Don’t just stand there, do you want to die!? —‘13 Bolts’!”

A monster that was closing in on me from the side was crushed by a concentrated volley of Magic Arrows.

Snapped back to reality by Marī’s sharp cry, I ran through the Dungeon again.

“Clair, I’m leaving Cindy to you!”

“Yes!”

“Marī! Protect Clair! I’m going in!”

Recklessly, Alex was charging into the monster horde alone.

He probably intended to draw their attention to himself and buy time, but no matter how skilled Alex was, fighting like that would quickly exhaust him. On the run, I pulled my sword from the monster’s carcass. I realized I had thrown away my Crossbow and the Baggage on my back and was charging forward with nothing but my body.

My vision narrowed sharply.

I tightly gripped the Hilt.

I shouted.

Putting my entire being into it.

I brought the blade down on the monster that was about to engulf the flames. As if in response to my will, the Blade was once again enveloped in a faint light, and the Slash I unleashed tore through the darkness like a single Meteor.

+++

# **69 - Dungeon Attack! (3)**

My ears were ringing terribly. It was because I had been repeatedly subjected to the grotesque shrieks of the Monsters, those hideous figures kneaded together out of human forms. My throat was raw. Every time I breathed, a painful sensation, like my lungs and throat being scrubbed with a Tawashi (a stiff scrubbing brush), shot through me. I wanted to stop breathing. My arms felt heavy. My legs were like lead. I wanted to throw everything away immediately and lie down on this cold floor. The cold air crawling up from the ground wrapped around my entire body like a gentle embrace.

“…Tch!! HaaAAAAH!!”

I expelled a gust of air to shake off the temptation of death.

I forcibly subdued and moved my twitching muscles with sheer willpower.

A blast of wind grazed my cheek. It was a hair’s breadth away. I hadn’t intentionally dodged it.

Guarded by luck, I finally closed the distance. I plunged into the wide-open space and, with that momentum, scrambled up the monster’s body. I brought my sword down from an Overhead Stance with all my strength, aiming for its crown.

A shriek. A tremendous sound that vibrated throughout my entire body.

My reason spurred on my mind and body, which were about to cringe.

—Not yet. They’re still aiming for you.

I knew it.

I quickly jumped off the monster before its entire body—which had lost its shape, like a broken thread or melting ice—could completely collapse. A few moments later, several tentacle-like arms pierced the space where I had just been standing. There was no time to rest.

—They cannot forgive the living.

Marī and the others appeared in the corner of my vision. Marī, who was sheltering the two immobile figures, clearly looked pale. Her body must have consumed a vast amount of Magic Power from continuously casting spells. In this world, the depletion of Magic Power leads to a threat to life. Yet, she, who should understand that more than anyone, continued to unleash a storm of Magic Arrows with relentless valor. She was literally sacrificing her life to protect Cindy and Clair.

Clair seemed to be focused on treating Cindy.

A pure glow, as if tearing through the Dungeon’s darkness, emanated from her hands. She seemed to be casting a considerably high-level Healing Magic. That meant Cindy’s condition must have been quite poor. If Clair hadn’t given up, there was still hope for Cindy, but performing treatment in the middle of a battlefield meant the conditions were extremely unfavorable.

I should abandon her. There were times when struggling was futile.

Hadn’t I always survived by doing just that?

Cindy was finished. Give up this time.

Your comrades would stay to die unless you abandoned her.

My experience as an adventurer who survived was making a cold, rational judgment.

I swung my arm hard, fighting against that thought.

A silver flash tore through the monster’s abdomen.

Its internal organs, drenched in black sludge, splashed onto the floor. Perhaps because the laws of life had been distorted, despite having suffered a clearly fatal wound, the monster still reached out with its arm—toward my comrades behind me—and gnashed its teeth. I thrust a finishing blow into it.

—They desire that soft, warm, blood-circulating flesh.

…Ah, I understood.

I realized the true nature of the Aberrant Monsters. I was forced to realize it.

A tattered, broken blade was thrust near a twisted arm. It must have been the end of someone who struggled to crawl out of the horrific mire of Rotting Flesh but ran out of strength. A familiar metal fragment hung from one of the necks growing out of the lump of flesh. That was the Adventurer’s Proof. They were Moving Headstones.

The graveyard, pregnant with the dead, was attacking the living who had visited this place.

That one. And that one. Once I realized it, it was obvious.

I could see that the Monsters had absorbed the corpses of many adventurers.

The particularly large monster, with a long, reptile-like physique, was extraordinarily abnormal.

The adventurers who had lost their way in the Dungeon were embedded in its body. Their final expressions were all hideously contorted with Lamentation and Suffering. The hollow, cave-like eye sockets stared at us with resentment.

“Still alive.”

“Why are you alive?”

“Why are you alive!?”

“Die! Die! Die!”

“You should die quickly too!”

They spewed curses of Resentment and Grief, as if they couldn’t stand our existence.

Black bubbles gurgled and dispersed, spreading a foul odor. It was all an Auditory Hallucination. The dead do not speak. Furthermore, there was no way that they, who had become mere lumps of flesh, still possessed will. The Wanderers absorbed by Marra’s Curse. That was the true nature of the black, ugly monsters.

The moment I realized various things, a sight suddenly jumped into my opened vision, leaving me speechless. There was one individual with a disproportionately small hand growing out of it. It wailed with a high-pitched cry, unlike the other monsters. It continued to emit shrieks filled with Sorrow more than Resentment. That was. That was—!!

“What in the hell is this!!”

I could feel violent rage raging in my chest.

That looked exactly like a Child’s Hand!

—Yes. These are the pitiful beings whose flesh and soul were defiled. This is the ultimate form of the people of Marra, brought about by the curse.

“Tch!! Stop fooling around!”

Why did they have to suffer such a terrible fate?

A Woman was absorbed into the Aberration while hugging what looked like her child, protecting it. The expression of her final scream was still plastered on her face. Her mouth, wide open as if splitting, cried out in Grief. The voices of Resentment chained together. They bleated with thick, turbid voices. A chilling Nightmare Chorus. As the monster lumbered and crawled toward me, shaking its massive body and crying out with a voice mixed with a baby’s Temper Tantrum, it slammed a bulging, warped, log-like arm down with furious speed.

Unforgivable.

My sword, its radiance intensified in response to my anger, cleanly cleaved the monster’s powerful arm, which had been swung down carelessly, right in half. An Iron Rank adventurer should not be capable of such a feat. Strength exceeding the limits of the human body was being drawn out by the magma-like emotions boiling in my gut.

Was this the true worth of Leveling Up?

A feeling of Omnipotence and Exhilaration enveloped my entire body.

It was no exaggeration to say that I had acquired the Cheat Ability I had longed for.

However, an intense anger, powerful enough to overshadow even that feeling, filled my entire being.

In the underground of Marra, which was destroyed 100 years ago.

They had been wandering in this darkness all this time. Using the hands they reached out for salvation to crush fellow citizens and adventurers, absorbing them as part of themselves. Perhaps the reason these creatures gathered in the Sanctuary’s protected area was that—even after becoming Aberrant Monsters that only scattered death and curses—they had always dreamed of being Saved.

Since the day Marra perished. In this very place. Even their small wishes were trampled, and they were transformed into the Curse itself, destined to last for all eternity. They were the residents of an Unending Nightmare.

Witnessing such horrific Malice firsthand.

How could I not be enraged!!

The Monsters reached out with their hands one after another.

They were trying to turn my precious people into hideous monsters.

They were trying to incorporate them into this Chain of Curses.

I absolutely could not allow that to happen.

I stood in front of the Aberrant Monster that had swallowed countless adventurers.

Its raised upper body was like that of a Dragon. A Cursed Dragon that devoured human life and hope. It let out an explosive roar, trembling its countless tentacle-like arms that grew all over its body. A roar accompanied by destructive power. A wall of air relentlessly slammed into my entire body.

“…Tch!!”

It was as if I were facing a real Dragon.

There was no doubt that this creature had devoured many veteran adventurers.

The concrete image of death stripped away all the heat from my body.

If I surrendered my knees to the surging despair, even my will to resist would be swallowed whole.

And there must have been adventurers who perished without even exchanging blows with it.

“Hah, hah… Who says I’ll give up! I won’t give up!”

I could repel the crushing pressure because an endless rage, powerful enough to completely overshadow all the rising fear, surged up from the depths of my chest. Flames swirled like a storm. The feeling, swelling like a cumulonimbus cloud booming with thunder, became a Torrent that swept away all my hesitation.

The sword entrusted to me by Hagen was imbued with a blue, lightning-like glow on its Blade.

It was the same technique Alex used to wrap his sword in flames. A skill that significantly enhanced attack power by imbuing a weapon with Magic Power—Magic Enchantment. Why I was able to use a skill I hadn’t learned was a minor question. Since this power awakened, even my clumsy Swordplay had become an effective strike against the monsters. That was what mattered now.

I pointed the Sword’s tip at the face of the fake Dragon, glaring back into its hollow eye sockets.

“I’ll end your nightmare!”

Another roar. But I didn’t flinch.

The slamming Gale, the Malice, the Despair.

“I’ll cut it all down with my own hands!”

I firmly gripped the glowing Sword with both hands and leaped out like an arrow.

To save my comrades. To sever the Curse that infested Marra.

I challenged the powerful enemy that mimicked the form of the Strongest Creature.

+++

# **70 - Zarumen’s Challenge**

The creature, shaking its massive body far larger than a cow or an elephant, drew its head back significantly. Then, whipping its neck like a lash, it launched a sweeping attack. The movement looked slow and deliberate, but the reality was the opposite. A drop of several meters went from full height to zero in the blink of an eye.

“Tch!!”

Timing it carefully, I took one large leap to duck under the attack.

The Dragon’s neck grazed my side with a tremendous roar. The swirling wind and the shockwave transmitted through the ground spoke of the immense destructive power hidden within that giant body.

It was probably like a Motorcycle or Passenger Car charging in with Killing Intent.

Likely, a direct hit would instantly obliterate me.

I doubted whether my body, enhanced by Leveling Up, could withstand it.

The equipment on the corpses of the predecessors who had challenged this creature and failed were all warped, torn, and rotten like rags. Since even metal armor suffered that fate, my own gear probably wouldn’t serve any purpose as protection.

In my previous life, I often played high-difficulty games where an enemy’s single attack could mean instant death, but for that to become reality and befall me now…

“This is too damn tough!!”

In games, I could challenge without fear of failure repeatedly. Because I could retry even if I died, I could boldly face any strong enemy or any disadvantageous situation.

But in reality, I couldn’t afford to fail. I only had one shot.

I had no choice but to somehow make the most of this One Chance.

“First, a strike!”

I dove into its chest and quickly slashed its torso.

“Oooohhh!!”

I felt the impact.

The Blade, emitting a pale blue light, easily sliced through the Dragon’s thick physique. It effortlessly cut away the black flesh that armored the Dragon, like a heated knife cutting through butter.

The sound of the blade sinking deeply into the festering flesh transferred to my hand.

To be honest, it was repulsive. Was it because that thing was an incarnated Curse? Simply being close to it made me feel dread and a chill. I had a certain conviction that the act of plunging my sword into the Curse was somehow whittling away at something inside me.

“…So, fighting it drains me even more. That’s just vicious!”

I was constantly fraying my nerves to avoid one-hit-kill attacks, and I lost spirit and stamina every time I struck the blade into it. By the time I noticed the abnormality, it was too late. The prey was successfully being stripped of its means of resistance.

“A Long Battle is a disadvantage.”

First of all, I didn’t know how long my stamina would last.

The Magic Enchantment that boosted my sword’s power was only being done unconsciously. If the skill activation were to break off for any reason, that would be the end. I had no other effective means of attacking the monster.

I felt a slight sensation of my strength draining away.

This was probably my Magic Power and my Life Force. It was natural, since I was continuously releasing Magic Power through the sword as a medium. Gradually, but surely, my limit was approaching.

The sense of death rapidly closing in.

The mouths of the Wanderers seemed to be smiling.

“Seriously, this is just too tasteless…!”

I muttered softly and tightly gripped my sword.

I crouched low and dashed forward, once again getting close to the monster.

A piercing roar. A threat.

The Dragon spread its countless arms as if unfurling Wings.

Numerous Tentacle Arms lunged straight at me.

“Are you serious!?”

Contrary to the surprise that involuntarily escaped me, the light in my sword didn’t even flicker.

If anything, the sharpness of the glow in the sword intensified further.

“Haaaaah!!”

I drew a pale blue arc in the air with a Rending Shout. The area of the rain-like tentacle attack was wide, but thanks to the simple trajectory, I had enough time to dodge while sweeping them away. The tentacles severed by my sword instantly dissipated on the spot with a sound like water evaporating.

“I can do this!”

The Attribute residing in my sword seemed to be effective against the monster.

“I’m going to push straight through!”

I cut down another individual that approached from the side, dodged a Tentacle Arm that shot out like a spear, and a powerful, precisely aimed strike from the tail, swung down from above, only grazed my nose thanks to me twisting my body.

I took a step. Swung the sword. Another Step.

The benefits of Leveling Up had drastically improved my physical abilities.

My body moved exactly as I willed it to.

“Ooooohhh!!”

A flash. I sliced off one of the feet supporting the massive body.

“Daaaahh!!”

With a reverse cut, I severed the mass of arms that was closing in. There was no time to catch my breath. I immediately leaped back to avoid the thin, sharp tentacles that flew like arrows. I pressed forward, jumping several meters in a single breath. I sliced off another foot. The giant body wavered.

“Keep it coming!!”

I plunged my sword deep into its flank.

A shriek that shook the Dungeon echoed.

But, not yet. This thing wasn’t dead yet.

When I pulled out the sword, black bodily fluid gushed out of the wound.

Because of this, the body shrunk, shriveling up.

Simultaneously, the Dragon’s neck drooped down—

“There!!”

I swung the sword with all my might.

A full-power strike, as if scooping upwards or thrusting the sword into the heavens.

“Haa… haa… haa…”

It cleanly cleaved the Dragon’s thick neck.

The neck, thrashing from the force of the black blood erupting from the cross-section, scattered a rain of black blood, like the monster’s final death throes. Where the spray hit, my equipment made a sizzling, unpleasant sound. A thin wisp of smoke rose from the parts of my skin that were touched, and they stung with a sharp, throbbing pain.

I should leave the area as quickly as possible.

There was no reason to be struck by the black rain of the Curse.

I needed to leave this place fast.

Yet, contrary to my reason, my eyes couldn’t look away from the Dragon impersonator, which was still raining blood.

It was a premonition.

One could even call it a form of anticipation.

“I knew it.”

I didn’t know why I thought that.

Or why I felt that way.

“…Kah!?”

Soundless and too fast for the eye to follow. By the time I realized it, my body was flying through the air. My entire body slammed onto the ground, the world turned upside down, and a pain that felt like it was burning my nerves, a pain that made it a wonder my limbs weren’t torn off, seized me.

I had taken a Fatal Blow.

The reason I was still alive must have been that I instinctively assumed a defensive posture.

Unconsciously, or by instinct, I endured the invisible strike by using my sword and my left arm as a shield.

“Geho, Goho… Kah… spits!”

I spat out the red blood in my mouth.

And I glared at the enemy in front of me.

A Multi-Headed Snake. That was my first impression.

New Snakes were growing from the severed limbs and neck.

Ugly Snakes clad in scales of Human Bone.

“Ha, hahaha, I knew it… It pretends to be dead, but there’s a Second Form…”

It was reminiscent of the Yamata no Orochi, but its ugliness was on a whole other level.

The grown Snakes had several hands, and each one was gripping a spear or a sword.

The mismatched hands, the weapons, the bone armor, everything, everything, everything—!!

“Do you really, really hate humans that much—!!”

The Snakes, with arms growing like a centipede, attacked me as I yelled my rage. I wouldn’t run. I couldn’t run. My anger had reached its peak.

“OAAAAAAH!!”

A myriad of attacks, descending like an avalanche.

I roughly swept them away with a powerful, Magic-infused sword swing.

A fierce impact sound and shockwave assaulted my entire body. It was a scene as if the energy of the attacks themselves had collided, exploded, and dispersed.

Fragments of shattered weapons glittered like snow. I sliced a body, which had been significantly unbalanced by the collision of energy, clean in half.

However, the opponent wasn’t deterred by just that.

It launched a Wave Attack from the front, back, left, and right.

I searched for a way to counterattack while clashing with them using my Sword of Light.

“Zeh, Hah… At this rate, I won’t get anywhere…!”

I was surrounded, the creature maintaining a distance where I couldn’t escape.

When I tried to push forward to cut down one of them, I was fiercely blocked by flanking maneuvers.

I had never felt the truth of the phrase “Many Against Few” more keenly.

It seemed I was superior in sheer power.

The opponent must have noticed this, too, and intended to wait until I weakened, using evasive tactics.

It would have been better if it had just been a large monster. Did it think it had acquired Intelligence by growing human hands, despite its aberrant appearance? In reality, that was exactly why I was being cornered like this.

Even a desperate gamble wasn’t allowed.

The slowly creeping impatience began to dull my limbs.

No, that’s not it.

It was my body’s reaction time that was slowing down—

“—Zaryū, above!!”

“Tch!?”

I jerked my head up. I narrowly avoided the approaching white blade. The one who called my name allowed me to notice the stealthy, Vicious Blade. I was about to turn to the source of the voice—when a blast of hot wind, an undulating flame, rushed past me.

A reassuring weight slammed into my back.

“Hah-hah! Did I keep you waiting long?”

With his red hair fluttering like a Heat Haze.

The Blazing Sword Prince arrived with a flourish to save me from my predicament.

+++

# **71 - The Reached Horizon**

“Alex!!”

“I’ll take over from here. You rest over there!”

Alex’s voice, confident as always, was reassuring.

I felt like nodding in agreement without a second thought to his offer.

It seemed both my spirit and physical strength had long since reached their limit without me realizing it.

That’s likely why my arms and legs were no longer moving as I wished.

As expected, even the deception by my Level Up had its limits.

I did well.

Didn’t I do well against an opponent of a higher rank?

Now that Alex had arrived, I could finally relax.

The sensation of the strength draining out of my limbs.

The thread of tension snapped, and my arms and legs naturally lowered.

Upon closer look, both my weapon and body were battered.

I was no longer in a condition to fight.

I thought I should just leave the rest to Alex.

I was about to succumb to that sweet temptation.

…However, it was then that I suddenly realized something.

The presence I felt through my back.

It felt as small as a young girl’s. The back he leaned against mine was heaving violently up and down. While he tried to maintain his usual composure, he was desperately hiding his ragged breathing.

It was an obvious display of bravado.

Alex had just been fighting countless monsters alone.

He couldn’t possibly be un-fatigued. Yet, I hadn’t immediately noticed his lie.

“You’re an idiot.”

A whisper, barely audible.

Such a muttering escaped my lips.

Pathetic. Embarrassing. Frustrating.

The servile nature ingrained from years of being an Adventurer weakened my heart.

Yet, I was supposed to have wanted to change that part of myself!

“Alex.”

I wasn’t the old me anymore.

I already held the power to fight in my hands.

“I might be unreliable, but…”

I spurred my timid heart to action. My heart was beating fiercely. So, if the core of my chest was burning hot, I should be able to send enough heat to my cold limbs.

I clenched my hands once more.

The radiance dwelling in the blade still shone brightly.

I gritted my teeth and poured strength into my entire body.

I could still move. I could still fight. Nothing was broken yet.

“At least, let me protect your back!”

I spat out my weakness as a defiant challenge.

I was here to save my comrades. Not to be saved by them. When I told myself this, the trembling in my limbs stopped.

“Zaryū, you…”

Confusion and agitation transmitted through my back.

However, it was only for an instant.

Alex’s presence suddenly grew immense.

“Heh… ‘protect my back’, you say…”

The weight leaning against my back increased.

I felt a heat through my back, so hot I thought I might get burned.

A crimson flame-like heat was being transmitted from Alex.

“Then, I’ll rely on you.”

It was a faint whisper, like a breath near my ear. It was neither mockery nor flattery. It was a word of pure, unadulterated trust spoken through my back. A comforting resonance, as if we were connected from the depths of our hearts. It was what I had always wanted as an Adventurer.

“Let’s go, Zarumen!”

“Yeah!”

As Alex dashed forward, I followed right behind.

Alex leveled his flamberge, leaped in front of the enemy, and slammed a fierce, sweeping blow. It looked purely powerful, but it was a honed flash. It mowed down everything in its path—the weapons and shields held by the multi-armed creature, the bone scales, everything that stood in the way.

I couldn’t afford to be mesmerized by Alex.

I exploited the opening he created, rushed the enemy, and stabbed my sword of light deep into the inner parts where the armor had been stripped away. A shriek. The curse dissipated with a deafening screech.

It was hard to believe I had been struggling against it so much before.

I succeeded in easily defeating one.

However, I had no time to bask in the afterglow.

Turning around immediately, I saw Alex intercepting the attack of another creature that was right in front of us. I thought Alex would instantly swat it away, but he dropped to one knee on the spot.

“Ugh, damn it!!”

“Alex!”

He tried to push back, but it seemed his strength was insufficient. His flamberge wasn’t even wreathed in flame. Could he be so exhausted that even maintaining the magic enchantment was difficult? Another creature crept toward the immobile Alex. It was clearly aiming for his exposed flank.

“—You won’t!!”

I dropped my hips low, set my sword, and charged, putting my whole soul into a body check.

Collision. Shatter. A dull ache.

Unable to fully kill my momentum, I tumbled across the floor two or three times.

I quickly got up, readied my weapon, and surveyed my surroundings to assess the situation. My desperate body check had apparently succeeded in disrupting the balance of both the one pinning Alex down and the one trying to attack him, involving both serpent-like creatures.

“—Flame! Burn them to ashes!!”

Suddenly, scorching heat surged from the undulating blade of the flamberge.

Following Alex’s swordsmanship, it drew the horizon of dawn in the underground darkness. The two serpent-like creatures, cleaved together, struggled and writhed for a while but were eventually consumed by the flames, turning into black charcoal and ceasing to move.

“Phew… pant, huff… pant, huff…”

Alex knelt down, breathing heavily, heaving with his shoulders.

He held up a hand to stop me when I rushed to his side.

I noticed with a start. The next creature was closing in on us without a moment’s rest.

So that was it.

Alex trusted my words and put out his full effort, even knowing it was reckless.

I had to live up to that trust.

“…!! Light!!”

In my mind was the image of Alex from a moment ago.

I spun the words and swung my sword, trying to trace that image.

“Burn to ashes!!”

The light dwelling in my sword shone brightly, responding to my words.

I couldn’t unleash a slash that divided the world like Alex.

Nevertheless, in this dark underground, I could at least become a star that flashed for a moment.

The moment it shone strongly like the North Star, the blade of light in my hand severed the monster’s body, cutting through even the metal armor and shield it wore.

The next moment, I involuntarily collapsed to my knees.

“*Huff, huff, huff…!?”

I landed on my hands and knees, still gripping the sword.

I couldn’t breathe. My heart felt like it would burst. The sudden exhaustion that attacked me was like what you feel after running a full marathon. My vision swayed, and a headache pulsed. I recognized this terrible dizziness and these symptoms.

“Huff, huff… Th-this is, Magical Exhaustion, isn’t it…!”

It was probably a side effect of trying to imitate Alex’s technique.

I hadn’t intended to use it. I hadn’t even thought I could.

However, my body had naturally chased the phantom of Alex that was burned into my eyes. I was careless; now both of us were immobilized.

“You really are an idiot, aren’t you?”

A cold remark pierced me.

At the same time, countless arrows struck the body of the monster that was closing in on me. The monster tried to defend itself with the armor covering its body, but it could not stop the overwhelming number of magical arrows. Its body was crushed into pieces, leaving only a black stain on the floor.

“Try to learn some moderation, will you?”

“…I didn’t think I could actually do it.”

“Even more of an idiot.”

“…I have no words to argue with that.”

Marī, holding her staff, stepped in front of me to guard me.

“Cindy is safe.”

Marī answered before I could ask.

“Clair cast a barrier. That’s why we came to help.”

“Thank you.”

“No need for thanks; we’re comrades… but,”

Marī, who had been speaking in a detached tone, suddenly turned and glared at me.

“Don’t do anything reckless.”

“…!!”

She radiated a freezing aura that brooked no argument.

She was genuinely angry. Realizing this, I could only silently nod my head.

“Your skills haven’t dulled, even after a long time out of the field, Marī.”

If the benefit of Level Up could turn a person’s will into reality.

The morning sun shone into the darkness of the Marra Dungeon.

A noise, neither a scream nor a shriek, rang directly in my brain.

Anger, hatred, sorrow. A sound warning of something. The entity that had continually blasphemed life was now regretting its own existence. My blood boiled at its wickedness. This was the one thing that absolutely had to be ended here.

“Woooooohhhhhhh!!”

Ignoring everything, I focused my will into the hand gripping the sword of light.

“Vanish right hereeeeeee!!”

A notably stronger burst of light slid down the blade.

It was literally a strike that gambled with my entire being.

Darkness returned to the Dungeon.

The light I held in my hand vanished without a trace.

A silence, as if everything had disappeared into nothingness, descended.

The voices of resentment hating the living, the ominous sounds of life being sucked away, the rancid smell of rotting souls… everything was gone. The Curse of Marra had been completely extinguished.

Witnessing this, I felt a strange sense of comfort.

It was slightly different from a feeling of refreshment.

It was a sensation as if my chest was empty.

\<\<Warning. Severe damage to the Magical Power Supply Organ>>

Suddenly, a beep echoed in my brain.

A synthesized voice calmly announced to me.

\<\<Activity limit reached. Forcibly terminating>>

Something snapped inside me.

Someone was calling me.

I didn’t understand the words at all, but the tone of the voice made it clear that they were worried about me.

It was a sensation as if I were underwater.

I hadn’t changed at all.

I had suppressed it all the time. My reason always held me back, insisting that I should be serious. While I wouldn’t deny that being serious was a good thing, it was also true that I had always kept a lid on my other desires and pretended not to see them.

I wanted to succeed in my job, fuck hot women, and eat delicious food.

It was vulgar, but it was also my genuine, honest desire.

If I died, everything was over.

I couldn’t fuck women anymore.

I couldn’t eat. I wouldn’t succeed in my job.

All that remained after death was deep regret.

Floating in this void, I would only harbor bitterness until my heart faded away.

There was no continuation. No path ahead. No chance for atonement.

That’s why everything was meaningless, yet I still spoke of my regrets.

Just one more time, one more time, I wanted to live and redo that moment.

I was sick of my own ugliness and shallowness for only thinking such things. But when I thought that this was my true, unvarnished self, I felt an inexplicable sense of resignation. I was disgusted with my insignificant self.

I recognized the person who was acting strangely familiar with me.

It was the God who reincarnated me into another world that time.

The orientation I recognized and the God’s position aligned. In an instant, my eyes spun, and I fell heavily to the ground. While feeling a slight dizziness, I felt a comforting sensation from the ground I stepped on after a long time.

As expected, it must be “just the way it is.”

I decided to accept it immediately.

For now, I pulled up a chair that had suddenly appeared in front of me and sat down.

A chair, a desk, and a tea set. Fine furnishings had appeared out of nowhere. I realized that the setting was two of us having an elegant tea party in a garden gazebo bathed in warm sunlight. The desolate void had suddenly transformed into a vibrant space with the God’s appearance. I vaguely sensed that this was precisely what a God’s Blessing must be like.

Ah, nostalgic. I felt that this fragrance was the brand I used to drink in my Previous Life.

I couldn’t remember the name or the taste, but I still remembered the scent.

“Yes.”

“…I see.”

“I understood the words, but I haven’t quite consented yet… just a little… give me some time…”

“Ah, I don’t mind.”

There have always been stories of evil gods, like Aramitama or Eikibyōgami.

I knew that the concept of a God couldn’t be simply divided into good and evil.

But, even so.

I had a feeling that I didn’t want to recognize that thing—which indiscriminately cursed and killed the people of Marra and preyed on Adventurers lost in the Dungeon—as a God. That thing was definitely not something as grand as a God… it was something that strongly reeked of human ugliness, or rather, the concentrated foulness of dark emotions like malice and killing intent. While I was muttering and updating my internal definition of God, the God in front of me suddenly let out a loud laugh.

“Really, I wonder what you see and how you see it with those eyes of yours.”

Saying that, the God stifled a laugh.

Three cards were presented in front of me.

They were the same cards as the ones that determined my reincarnation destination that time.

“Not an option.”

He flatly refused.

In short, I would be reincarnated into yet another world.

I would receive a new life there, and perhaps I would recall the memories of my Previous Life again… and then, I would regret it after dying, just like today. I would struggle, writhe, and frantically try to gather everything. And then I would still mourn.

“Everything in the world is connected.”

The God spoke as if to appease me.

“The world revolves, cycles, and repeats.”

He poured milk into the coffee and stirred it with a teaspoon.

White and black swirled and eventually mixed into one.

He scooped up a sugar cube with the spoon, dropped it in, and stirred again.

“It’s good to keep revolving around the same spot many times. Until the white and black completely blend together.”

A voice that was worried about me.

# **74 - Zarumen The Adventurer**

Let’s rewind time to when the white blade of light I unleashed dyed the dungeon, cleaving the curse that infested Marra—what the God referred to as a god-powered being—in two.

“What was that light!?”

Marī, temporarily blinded by the intense light, cried out.

When I timidly opened my eyes in the sudden silence and darkness, the dreadful monsters had vanished without a trace. It was so complete that I suspected it all might have been a hallucination. The proof that it was real lay in the battle scars scattered everywhere and the sight of my comrades, wounded, exhausted, and collapsed.

Leaning my weight on my staff, I slowly moved my feet forward.

Marī, who had managed to reach us, immediately checked on their safety. Alex had severe bruises, but his breathing was calm, and his expression was relaxed. She sighed in relief, figuring his life wasn’t in danger.

The cause was excessive consumption of magic power, which led to magic power depletion, and the subsequent necrosis of the magic power supply organ due to being overburdened. Magic power in this world is life force. You could substitute it with stamina or mental energy. In a game analogy, the underlying source for both HP and MP is considered the same. Just as one dies when HP runs out, one dies when MP runs out.

Even for an Elf who had lived a thousand years, it would be impossible, let alone for a mere human, a simple Adventurer, to have enough magic power.

I apparently used my life force to substitute for the insufficient magic power.

As a result of continuing to push my body further to squeeze out what was still lacking, my body completely broke down.

≪Warning. Severe damage to the magic power supply organ≫

≪Activity limit reached. Forcing shutdown≫
