She, who had the keenest sense of life force among the Party, instantly perceived my condition was abnormal.

—Even with the secret art of resuscitation, the chance of saving him was one in ten thousand. That’s what I thought.

Nevertheless, she complied with Marī’s request and applied healing magic to me.

Strangely, my physical injuries rapidly improved thanks to Clair’s recovery magic. Marī and Alex found a glimmer of hope in this. However, Clair shook her head.

“…Unless Senpai’s soul returns here, healing an empty vessel won’t bring him back to life. There are spells to save those on the verge of death, but there are none in this world to call back those who have crossed the threshold…”

“…Are you giving up on Zaryū?”

“!!…I won’t give up!! I don’t want to give up!!”

And so, driven by Marī’s outburst, Clair reportedly kept using recovery magic on my body while crying great floods of tears. She had just finished treating Cindy. She must have been intensely fatigued and drained. Yet, even knowing it would likely be futile, she couldn’t stop casting recovery magic.

I apparently vomited blood several times after that.

It was due to broken bones—a side effect of the heart massage. The injuries would be healed by Clair’s recovery magic. And then, after a while, they would break again. She would heal them. This was the cycle, apparently.

—Also, the reason Senpai was naked was… because of the blood he vomited and his clothes getting dirty during the fight, and definitely not for any ecchi purpose.

Ah, yeah. Got it, got it.

Anyway, they continued the resuscitation through heart massage and the regeneration of my body through recovery magic until I woke up.

—And that brings us to the present.

---

“…Where is Cindy?”

“Asleep.”

Well, that figured. She was seriously injured.

Upon closer look, her bruises had spread even more.

“You say that, but even Cindy, after waking up, was selflessly helping us by taking out water, food, and potions from your gear to distribute as needed, and even wiping your sleeping body.”

“Alex! You didn’t have to say that!”

Cindy smacked Alex across the face with her palm.

Alex’s face showed irritation, but even he was apparently too exhausted to move a finger. He simply snorted unhappily, leaning against the wall.

Marī and Clair were the same.

They were equally exhausted, barely able to move.

Seeing the four of them safe, I finally breathed a sigh of relief.

“I’m truly glad everyone is alive.”

“That’s our line! Idiot! Zaryū, you idiot!!”

“…You’re right about that.”

I accepted Cindy’s curses with grace.

Having heard what happened after I lost consciousness, I bowed my head to them again.

“Thank you, everyone.”

Smiles appeared on their weary faces. The gentle expressions were soon overcome by sleepiness and melted away. Even Cindy, who had looked energetic, slumped to the floor as if all strength had drained from her body and began to snore.

I wrapped each of them with the blankets we had brought so their bodies wouldn’t get cold on the dungeon floor.

“You seem to be doing well.”

“…Yes, thanks to you.”

The one who spoke to me was Bernkatze, one of the Libra Marquis’s knights.

A dubious tone was mixed in his voice.

“I also witnessed you dead with my own eyes… Honestly, I can’t believe you are alive and moving now.”

Bernkatze and the knights were considerably exhausted from the battle with the monsters.

They had many injured and quite a few casualties. It seemed they barely managed to win by striking hard when the other monsters’ movements slowed down after I cleaved the boss of the curse.

Afterward, seeing Alex and the others utterly broken but desperately trying to revive me, he reportedly advised them to stop the pointless effort but was ignored. So, he decided to let Alex do as he pleased, reorganized the unharmed personnel, and stood guard over the area.

“If the young master had continued the resuscitation until he collapsed because of you, I would have torn your body to shreds. You understand that even if the young master resented me, his life is more important than your corpse, don’t you?”

Oh, that’s scary. His tone was serious.

This guy was the type who smiled sweetly while chasing you with a weapon.

“It’s good that things worked out safely for us both.”

“Haha, y-yeah, I guess so.”

It was too much trouble to find the right words, so I just gave a vague laugh.

“…Who exactly are you, really?”

I felt his gaze fixed directly on me.

I couldn’t tell what his expression was, as his knight’s helmet was still down.

His eyes had a complex color, suggesting suspicion and interest simultaneously.

“I wish I knew that myself.”

So, I confided my honest feelings.

“I’ve been an Adventurer, stuck at Level 1, and now I’m fighting a huge battle against a monster deep inside a dungeon. I picked up the life I’d dropped and am now sharing joy with my comrades again… Tell me, what do I look like to you?”

“…”

After a moment of thought, Bernkatze replied.

“A frivolous, shady man who’s deceiving the young master. I’m envious and intensely jealous that someone of unknown origin like you is so favored by him. And you even exchanged an intimate kiss… Ugh! How disgusting! And yet, how enviable!”

Bernkatze’s voice trembled, his fist shaking as he held it out to me.

His tone was forceful, clearly demonstrating the sincerity of his feelings.

“…Wait, so, I did… with Alex…”

For the several hours until I woke up, Alex had apparently kept performing artificial respiration and heart massage on me. Oh no. Did that mean I kissed him more times than Marī and the others? I exchanged deep breaths, an intimate kiss, with those faintly shapely, elegant lips so many times. No, I shouldn’t think about it too much. My brain was about to break in multiple ways.

“Hey, are you planning to assault the young master while he sleeps? I’ll execute you! Huh?”

“No, I won’t! Put away that dangerous thing! Alex and I are both men, don’t say such creepy things!”

“Huh? Does his aesthetic look care if he’s a man? What’s wrong with two men? You look like a hesitant seme! Do you think you can mislead me now with a non-care appeal?! Since you’re from a brothel, is your technique truly amazing?! What kind of tricks did you use to deceive the young master! Come on, spill everything right here!!”

“Agh, what the hell, you’re suddenly so gross!? Alex and I aren’t like that!!”

To escape Bernkatze’s out-of-control, abnormal interrogation, I decided to temporarily leave the spot.

“…Seriously, I thought he was strange, but is that his kind of hobby…”

I don’t intend to criticize anyone’s hobbies, but I’m straight.

Besides, I didn’t feel anything for Alex.

“…I don’t feel anything about him, right?”

Strangely, my face felt hot when I thought about Alex.

A series of Alex’s sexy poses surfaced and disappeared in my mind. The image of him behind my eyelids carries a somewhat feminine silhouette, and well, unexpectedly.

“Ah, right, Alex is my life-saver!”

He’s also an admirable figure as an Adventurer!

His strength, his subtle kindness, his coolness—that charm that made even a man fall for him was what’s great about Alex! …Yes, a wholesome relationship!

“Haha, it’s a good thing Alex is a man. If he were a girl, I’m confident I wouldn’t be able to look him in the face anymore.”

I shook my head, trying to dispel the confusing feelings.

Then, I shifted my focus. I was alone in a deserted place.

It was the perfect time to check something.

“—Oh, Light.”

I inhaled slowly and called out.

A small globe of light floated right into my hand.

I gripped it tightly, and it turned into a single sword.

The blade of light was about 50 centimeters long. A slender, one-handed sword.

The light crackled and spilled from the edges.

“Oops.”

Panicked that it couldn’t maintain its shape, I deactivated the power.

With just a thought, the blade of light instantly vanished into the void.

“…As expected, using a sword hilt or something as a medium makes it more stable.”

The advanced skill of Magic Imbuement was Magic Weapon.

As the name suggested, it’s a skill that gave form to magic power and handled it as a weapon. It’s said to be one of the secret techniques that only a handful of veteran Warriors, those especially skilled in handling magic power, could acquire.

The convenience of being able to produce a weapon anywhere, as long as you had magic power. The reliability of being able to damage troublesome, insubstantial monsters with a weapon imbued with magic power, and the fact that a Magic Weapon, being magic power itself, was expected to deal higher damage in actual combat than an attack merely clad in magic power. Of course, it also possessed exceptional performance as a weapon. It’s like shaping offensive magic into a weapon, so its power was immense. The only drawback was probably the fuel efficiency, as it seemed to consume magic power excessively.

“In my case, I lack the fundamentals in the first place.”

This was originally a secret technique acquired by a Warrior who had continuously used Magic Imbuement and reached the level of mastery.

I, who acquired it driven by emotion during battle without the necessary know-how, seemed to have firmly grasped the sensation of weaponizing magic power, but I apparently had no idea about the trick to retaining the magic power I’ve released in the shape of a weapon.

I could probably maintain it for a dozen seconds if I tried hard, but I don’t think I can create a sword of light with the destructive power, strength, or size I had at that time.

“Speaking of which, Hagen said his sword contained Mithril… The reason I could suddenly use Magic Imbuement is… I was helped by Hagen again.”

The staple fantasy material, Mithril, exists in this world too.

Most other metals had a property that blocks magic power to a greater or lesser extent. Hence, Mithril was a rare metal with the unusual property of “easily conducting magic power,” and it was highly valued by Adventurers as a material that was extremely compatible with the Magic Imbuement skill.

Hagen, who was apparently a very capable veteran Adventurer.

A Mithril weapon was by no means cheap. On the contrary, it’s such an item that it’s valued as a portable piece of wealth for an Adventurer. It has enough value to support a comfortable life for a while as an asset after retirement.

Why he entrusted such a thing to me. I couldn’t guess his heart. Nor should I. I believe what matters is whether the one who was entrusted with it was able to accomplish what they should. …Therefore, I decided that by protecting my comrades from that monster, I fulfilled the “thing I should do” that I received from Hagen.

“…If I don’t think that way, I can’t excuse breaking the weapon…”

Reporting to Hagen when I got back to town was already stressing me out. Joy, anger, sorrow, pleasure. Whatever expression he greeted me with, my heart was likely to be deeply wounded. If someone told me Hagen would be more upset, that might be true, but—

Speaking of equipment.

What I was wearing now was Alex’s spare clothes that the knights brought. My equipment was also a mess from the fight… some of it was ripped to shreds during the resuscitation. I wanted to refuse, but I couldn’t continue adventuring naked.

Was this silk? It felt nice against the skin. No loose threads.

This was the first time I’ve worn such high-quality clothes since my reincarnation. It reminded me that the quality I took for granted in my previous life was a super-luxury item in this world.

“Previous life, huh…”

I recalled the exchange with God.

The smell of coffee and tea I sensed then. A nostalgic scent that stirred memories and evoked a feeling of homesickness.

“…But I wished to return to this world. I strongly wished to come back to life.”

What about when I died in my previous life?

I felt like I easily accepted death. If I had accepted reincarnation as a matter of course, I should have simply accepted a new reincarnation this time too. But the reason I didn’t was—

“Ratori, Marī, and Shāri tied me to this world.”

My connections with them shattered any sense of ‘graceful acceptance’ within me.

Looking back, it was the same during the battle. Their existence was the support for my heart even in the toughest moments. Whether it’s because I impregnated them—I didn’t know. But I was so worried about how they would live if I died here, if I left this world after death. I was terribly frustrated by the thought of my absence.

“Did I not have such connections in my previous life… I think I had close friends, colleagues, and family… but it’s strange.”

I died protecting a stranger.

I had absolutely no regrets about that.

I had no hesitation in risking my life.

“But now, it’s different.”

I had no hesitation in risking my life.

But losing my life… I didn’t want to do that anymore.

“I will live through this world!!”

That was a vow to myself. Having gained the cheat ability called Level, I can turn my entire life, even my own life force, into power if I have the will. That means I can easily cross the boundary between life and death.

If I faced a difficulty and didn’t have the real power to overcome it.

I would try to overcome the danger by using my life as collateral. I can do it.

But I was not guaranteed to survive the next time.

I only had one life.

Even if there was a system of reincarnation and the concept of life continued uninterrupted across time and space, the story of Adventurer Zarumen’s life was written only once.

“I will live to the fullest. As an Adventurer. As Zarumen—”

I was a reincarnator.

I might have looked like I’d adapted to this world, but my feelings were still unsettled.

But from now on.

“I am Adventurer Zarumen!”

No one heard it. I was not making them listen. Just in the silent underground, in the dungeon, I loudly declare to myself.

I vowed to live my second life.

To the fullest, this time.

+++

# **75 - Descendants Of Marra**


…Well, it’s fine that I got caught up in the moment and made that declaration.

It’s fine. Yeah. I was still young.

At least since I was reincarnated, I was still young… Yeah.

I fanned my blushing cheeks with my hands, overcome by a delayed sense of shame, and tried to shift my focus to what to do next.

“First, should we continue to explore the dungeon or not?”

It seemed that the knight order was also divided on this.

The damage sustained in the last battle was severe.

Both the Adventurers and the knights were badly beaten.

Only about 30% of the knights’ forces were unharmed; the other half were severely wounded or dead, and the remaining half had their will to fight completely broken. It’s no wonder. They had witnessed their comrades being absorbed by monsters and seen them melting away from the black bodily fluid, going through a terrible ordeal.

In fact, it’s probably because they were highly trained that the damage wasn’t worse. In a panic horror story, it’s a kind of trope that panic spreads, leading to the annihilation of a military unit or a team.

Even returning the combat-incapable personnel outside would require a considerable amount of manpower. Continuing the exploration by dividing the remaining knight forces wouldn’t be very rational.

Our group also suffered immense damage.

Most of the equipment and tools we brought were used up.

There were many items for which we had no spares. The injuries and fatigue also had a major impact.

“It’s unfair that I’m the one who’s completely fine after dying and coming back to life.”

It’s not as if any injury was fully healed by a return from death.

Alex, Clair, Marī, and Cindy. Thanks to their devoted healing efforts, my body was completely mended. That’s all there was to it. The bone fractures and organ damage from the heart massage were all healed by Clair’s healing magic. Any brain damage was probably zero, thanks to the artificial respiration and healing magic.

“Yo, ho, ha!”

Just for the sake of trying, I moved my body.

I kicked off a wall and a pillar, and leaped. My body, lightly jumping, reached the ceiling, and after a light touch with my hand, I landed softly on the ground. With my body’s enhanced performance from leveling up, I could land by simply bending my knees to absorb the impact, without needing to take a special defensive posture.

“My body moves just as I thought it would, and I don’t feel any discomfort anywhere.”

On the contrary, I felt like I was completely mastering the physical performance enhanced by the level up. I could intuitively tell what I could do with this body and what I couldn’t. I could instantly understand which path to take and what actions to perform to achieve a conscious goal.

“I see, this is indeed ‘the reward for defeating the God’.”

This was the new Blessing I was given: Clairvoyance.

You could also call it intuition. It seemed like a very convenient blessing.

And whether it’s the power of that blessing or not—though I felt like some force was at work—I believed we should continue to explore the dungeon.

This was the complete opposite of what my usual judgment, as Adventurer Zarumen, would be.

“The monsters born from Marra’s curse stayed here. There must be a reason why so many of them gathered… that’s probably it.”

The speculation was vague because it’s my own thought.

The Blessing of Clairvoyance didn’t just give you the answer… But we had explored this deep into the Marra Dungeon. We hadn’t made any notable discoveries along the way. It wouldn’t be wrong to think that the real thing is waiting ahead.

“In fact, there might be something around here…”

My eyes suddenly caught a part of the wall.

A circuit-like structure was visible just beyond a slight chip.

“…Are you serious?”

I approached the wall to examine it more closely.

“Oh, Light.”

I wondered if it was a good idea to use a magic weapon as a lantern.

As a retort popped into my head, I peered inside.

“…A distribution panel? It looks dangerous to touch directly… It’d be great if there was a console panel nearby.”

I recalled the time I escaped the dungeon before. The magic hologram console panel I could see through Marī’s magical tool. If I could operate that, I might be able to activate a hidden device around here. However, since I don’t have that magical tool with me, I wouldn’t even notice if it was there.

“Speaking of which, that magical tool of Marī’s looks like smart glasses. It’s like AR when you can see magic power with those glasses.”

≪Would you like to turn on AR function?≫

“Uh, yes.”

≪Understood. Activating AR function.≫

The synthesized voice in my head suddenly started speaking loquaciously.

≪Connecting to Marra's city network. Accessing AR function.≫

“No, no, no, wait, wait, wait!?”

≪Understood. Temporarily suspending operation.≫

“…Sorry, please resume the operation.”

≪Understood. Connection to the city database successful. Downloading AR data to the personal data storage area.≫

Wait a minute. What’s gotten into this guy?

You hadn’t shown up at all except during level-ups!

“Ah, I’ve got a hunch.”

This existence was even more mysterious than the God, but thanks to the Blessing of Clairvoyance, I seemed to have guessed the answer.

“You’re an AI, aren’t you?”

≪Affirmative. This unit is an independent life support unit, ADA.≫

What a cliché phrase.

≪It is an artificial spirit created to support the lives of Marra's citizens. It was also called an assistant AI.≫

“What did you say?”

≪It is an artificial spirit created to support the lives of Marra's citizens. It was also called an assistant AI.≫

No. That’s not it.

“…I have a lot of questions, but in short… you’ll support me?”

≪Affirmative. Data download is complete. Playing AR.≫

I temporarily abandoned my questions and decided to simply accept the help of the AI—ADA. What was important was whether I could use the AR function and explore the Marra Dungeon.

And the change was dramatic.

My vision was suddenly filled with color. The dungeon, which should have been shrouded in silent darkness, suddenly began to glow like a neon city.

“Turn it off once.”

The fluorescent glow that had filled my vision instantly vanished.

I see, so the dungeon wasn’t actually being illuminated by a dazzling light; it was only visible to me. This is definitely AR, augmented reality.

I had it turned on again. There were colorful letters and symbols.

They must hold some meaning.

“I can’t read them.”

I couldn’t read the language used in Marra.

In this world, a common language is mostly used, but there are also local languages used only by certain races and in specific regions. I was reminded again that it seemed the common language was not the main one used in Marra. However, I could infer some things from the combinations of colors and the flashing.

“A warning, maybe?”

≪Currently, an emergency declaration has been issued for the entire urban area of Marra. All citizens of Marra have been instructed to evacuate to underground shelters immediately.≫

“Since when… How much time has passed…?”

≪—Approximately 900,000 hours have passed since the declaration was issued.≫

“So, it’s been since Marra was destroyed… right?”

≪A search for the nearest evacuation location has been completed. Would you like to start navigation?≫

“No, not now.”

I sat down right there.

When I confronted that monster, I was trembling with rage. I burned with anger for the people of a distant past and was driven by a sense of righteous indignation that I had to sever that curse. I also saw the forms of the citizens who had become part of the curse. But it still felt like a distant scene.

“Marra’s destruction wasn’t over. It has continued from that day until today…”

Did that monster see the AR view?

The cruel sight of time passing. The endless nightmare in vivid detail.

The reason they were aiming for a certain place, even when a sanctuary stood in their way—

“…No one can be saved. Not like this…”

The desire, the wish, the prayer to protect the citizens of Marra was here.

They wanted to be saved, to survive, to not die. Such thoughts were oozing out.

Even though there was no one left alive in this city, the city itself was still living.

It was in terrible taste.

Absolutely terrible taste.

“I’m not good with this kind of thing…”

It was too heavy for me to bear alone.

I didn’t have the resolve to look into the truth.

Why me?

“…Hey, ADA. Am I a citizen of Marra?”

≪Affirmative. The right to own this unit is restricted to only first-class citizens of Marra. Therefore, you are undeniably a citizen of Marra.≫

I remembered the day I first visited Marra.

My conversation with Marī echoed in my mind.

“Is it something to be proud of, being a descendant of Marra, just because you have the blood?”

“Hmm… Even so, it’s something you’re born with. It’s hard to deny your blood.”

“…You’re right, you can’t change your birth.”

“I was a prostitute’s bastard, so I couldn’t belong to any community. I’ve never felt a blood connection or pride… That’s probably why I longed to be an Adventurer, a profession where you can make it if you have the strength… I want to prove that I am who I am.”

Marī talked to me about her longing for Marra.

In that conversation, when she asked me whether a descendant of Marra should be proud of its greatness, a homeland that was now destroyed… I saw myself in her, with my former life as a home I could never return to.

Because it resembled my own struggle of not feeling completely at home in this world.

That’s why I told Marī that she should become the person she wanted to be.

To not be a reincarnator, but a person born and living in this world.

I wanted to become Adventurer Zarumen.

That event was what gave me the strong motivation to think that.

I got embarrassed, made a joke to lighten the mood, and got scolded by Marī.

We even made up with a kiss.

“…And now I find out that I’m actually a citizen of Marra… Hahaha, what am I supposed to say to Marī…?”

A root I thought I had lost suddenly appeared.

I felt like I was suddenly bound by an intricate web, even though there should have been no ties in this world. My heart was in a complex fracture. But thanks to this, one thing made sense.

“That intense rage that welled up inside me… and that seemingly inexhaustible surge of magic power—it was because I was a descendant of Marra. That’s it.”

When I thought about it that way, everything fell into place. The pieces that were supposed to fit together finally did. It was a complex feeling, like the missing pieces of a puzzle with holes in it were all unexpectedly filled.

“I’ve avenged them… but it doesn’t really feel that way…”

I felt relieved but also perplexed.

The state of my heart right now was truly complicated and bizarre.

+++

# **76 - Speaking With One Voice**

I was lost in thought for a while, but I finally got tired of it.

“…Well, who I am and where I come from doesn’t matter. I’ve decided to become an Adventurer. I’ll become what I want to be and live the way I want to live.”

A barrage of shocking facts had rushed in, but ultimately, what I should do and what I want to do here are simple.

“Find Marra’s legacy and break Marī’s curse, right?”

The thought of Marī naturally energized me.

I stretched to relax the tension.

“ADA, answer me. If Marra’s city network is alive, can you identify the locations where monsters or threats to the citizens are occurring?”

≪Order confirmed, initiating search. —Complete. Displaying on MAP.≫

A translucent map floated in front of my vision.

And in it, countless red dots of light were lined up.

“Are all of these threats?”

≪Confirming numerous life forms without a citizen ID. They are presumed to be invaders from an enemy nation.≫

“Ah, I see. It’s recognizing the knights as enemies.”

≪Due to the significantly low energy supply to the city, only the patrol golems of the interception system are currently operational.≫

“They are people from a friendly nation that I brought here to aid Marra. Can’t you do something about it?”

≪—The issuance of guest accounts for visitors from outside the nation is limited to five people per citizen. To grant permission for a group or a military organization to stay, a special pass issued by the relevant government ministry is required. As the city is currently under a state of emergency, new applications cannot be processed.≫

“I see.”

So, even if the knights proceed, they’ll be blocked by the city’s defense system. It seems best to have them retreat to the surface for now, and for me and a small number of personnel to continue the exploration ahead.

“…By the way, ADA, why have you been silent all this time? As an independent life support unit—an assistant AI—couldn’t you have helped me sooner?”

≪—This unit is an independent life support unit, ADA. It is an artificial spirit created for the purpose of supporting the lives of the citizens and was fundamentally manufactured for operation within the city of Marra. Therefore, this unit is equipped with almost no functions to assist activities outside the city.

…Hence, if you ask 'why', I can only answer that I am not supposed to be used for purposes other than the intended ones.≫

“Are you angry? I’m sorry.”

≪This unit has its emotional programming omitted.≫

It’s strange that I felt like emotions were seeping out of its words.

But I generally understood. ADA became loquacious because this was inside the city of Marra.

“…By the way, what exactly were the level-ups and, you know… the confirmation of implantation?”

≪They are biological monitoring functions. They monitor changes in the contacted partner and are utilized as data to support the household registration, childbirth, and childcare of Marra citizens. Personal information is highly encrypted, and there will be no utilization for unintended purposes. Please rest assured.≫

The discussion suddenly jumped to a surprisingly advanced social welfare system.

I felt an unexpected shock for the umpteenth time.

≪The level-up announcement is a function to inform when an individual's total magic power reserve reaches a certain rank. By possessing high magic power, your rank as a Marra citizen increases. A higher rank leads to a richer life. Always be conscious of leveling up to aim for a better rank.≫

I see, so the level-up was monitoring the amount of magic power.

In other words, by having sex, ejaculating inside the partner, and getting them pregnant, my own magic power reserve was increasing—wait, what the hell is that?

“…Hey, is there no causal relationship between impregnating a partner and leveling up?”

≪There is none.≫

“No, but! Every time I leveled up, it was after ADA said implantation was confirmed!”

≪There is no relationship. Please stop. That is sexual harassment.≫

“I was called a sexual harasser by an AI!?”

I sank to my knees in shock.

I’ve lived honestly my whole life, even in my previous one, and yet I was being certified as a sexual harasser for the first time by an artificial intelligence. Ugh, this was a considerable mental blow…

“…So, implantation and level-up are separate phenomena, and ADA wasn’t doing anything, right?”

≪This unit is not implemented with functions to encourage conception, or to interpret far-fetched, baseless, nonsensical humor such as biological function enhancement linked to it.≫

“O-oh, well, sorry about that…”

Does this AI really have no emotions? The pressure was intense.

“I thought a lot of mysteries were solved, but new ones have emerged.”

In the first place, I had a feeling that the existence of this ADA was the Blessing given to me. In an isekai reincarnation, there are cheat abilities that support the protagonist’s journey, right? I thought it might be something like that.

Its true identity was completely different.

However, I clearly have a power that seems to be the Blessing of Impregnation Sex (tentative name).

This ability, which cannot be measured by common sense, remained a mystery in the end.

“It seems even the Blessing of Clairvoyance isn’t giving me any hints about this.”

A Blessing was an ability granted by the God of this world. Perhaps if I had my Blessing examined at a temple somewhere, I might find out which God granted what ability.

“…Oops, I got distracted. First, I should rejoin Marī and the others.”

I put a lid on my thoughts for now.

Mulling over it constantly won’t necessarily yield an answer.

I needed to focus on what needs to be done right now.

---

I gathered several representatives of the knights, including Bernkatze, and Alex’s Adventurer Party for a consultation.

I decided to keep secret the fact that I was a citizen of Marra—a descendant of Marra—for now.

I told them that Marra’s city functions were still alive after a century, that the defense system saw the knights as enemies, and that since I had obtained a guest account, there was a possibility that up to five people besides me could head further into the dungeon.

“Do you think we would believe such nonsense!? Most likely, a filthy ambition to monopolize the treasure has welled up in you!!”

I received a scathing criticism from one of the knights.

The others, though not voicing it, were also skeptical of my explanation.

“We heard that you defeated the boss of those black monsters, but we are also skeptical about that. It’s true that they suddenly weakened and began to melt, but we can’t judge if that’s related to defeating the boss. There’s no guarantee that they won’t appear again ahead. Isn’t it too dangerous to proceed with a small number of people?”

There were also constructive opinions from those who were skeptical but wanted to proceed cautiously.

“A small number is fine. We can select the remaining five people from among the knights who have the energy.”

“The priority should be to transport the wounded out of the dungeon as quickly as possible to receive treatment. Therefore, I have no objection to continuing the exploration with a small team.”

Some prioritized achieving results. Others cared for their comrades.

“It’s nothing!!”

Alex’s face flushed bright red, and he turned away with a Hmph.

It seemed I angered him again.

“…Didn’t you notice even now, you idiot…!!”

His small, muttered grudge did not reach my ears.

“Well, for an Adventurer that Alex admires, he must be incredibly skilled.”

“…You’re right. He’s probably slaying dragons for treasure in some dungeon right now.”

“Hahaha, that’s amazing. I want to be that successful someday, too.”

“…”

It seemed I gave the wrong answer again. Alex sulked and didn’t speak another word until the massage was over.

“—Yeah, I feel much better. It’s thanks to you sharing your magic power. Thank you, Zarumen.”

Alex stretched his arms and legs, checking his condition.

His complexion certainly looked much better.

“This is all I can do.”

“Hey.”

Alex’s eyes snapped open. He shoved me against the wall, striking both hands on the wall to box me in. I was confused by the sudden kabedon (wall-pin).

“Are you still unaware of it?”

“O-of what?”

“Zarumen! You are no longer a perpetually incompetent Adventurer! You defeated the monster that infested the Marra Dungeon, the curse that no one could defeat, with your own hands!”

I recognized the look in his eyes, tinged with frustration and anger.

It was the same as when Marī admonished me on horseback that day.

It seemed I had unconsciously repeated the same mistake as that day.

“You no longer have to worry about anyone else’s opinion. You won’t be scorned as perpetually incompetent… You can stand right beside me! I won’t let anyone complain! You don’t have to feel inferior! From now on, you’ll be with me, forever…!!”

“Alex, thank you. For caring about me.”

I smiled at Alex, who was choked up.

“I guess I’m not the weak person I was anymore.”

Perhaps Alex and the others suffered more than I did.

The frustration of having their comrade insulted and being unable to talk back. That must be an inexpressible feeling. And now, my own act of belittling myself is an act of betrayal and insult to the trust they placed in me.

“Honestly, I still don’t have the confidence to proudly stand tall, but… I’ll try my best to live up to your expectations, Alex.”

“…Good. Just make sure you work hard enough so I don’t get tired of you!”

His tone was full of sarcasm, but the smile he gave was genuinely delighted.

For a moment, I felt like Alex looked like a girl.

+++

# **80 - Short Break**

Wait, why did Alex look like a girl!?

“What’s wrong? You suddenly look troubled.”

“No, it’s nothing.”

No, I mean, I’ve had experiences countless times where I thought he had a beautiful face and skin, or where a glimpse of his profile suddenly made my heart skip a beat! The fact that he’s a man was confirmed with my own eyes when we bathed together, so there should be absolutely no room for doubt… Yet, the image of Alex as a woman was strangely overlapping the figure of Alex in front of me.

Was this a trick of the God?

I had a feeling the Blessing of Clairvoyance was doing unnecessary work.

“…Zarumen…”

Alex’s eyes were suspiciously moist.

I felt the distance between us was subtly closing.

—This was bad.

The Blessing of Clairvoyance, which I was just doubting, whispered that danger was approaching.

I completely agreed with it.

My sixth sense was also picking up the dangerous atmosphere hovering in this spot.

I felt the same amount of pressure as when I confronted the monster I had just defeated.

“A-Alex? Doesn’t something seem strange with you, too?”

“…Zarumen…”

Alex called my name, letting out hot, burning breaths.

His face was slowly but surely getting closer to mine. A man with a girl-like face was approaching, his lips trembling with an expression like a maiden in love.

Bad. This was bad. Extremely bad.

Following Marī and Clair, Alex was also acting weird.

It was obvious now that some undesirable component was mixed into the ointment.

The problem was that it seemed to be forcefully prying open a sexual fetish I kept tightly sealed. If the opponent were any other guy, I would simply beat him up without question and be done with it, but facing Alex, who had the looks of a beautiful girl, created a strange hesitation.

I should run away from this spot immediately.

The survival instinct ingrained in me from years of Adventuring life judged so.

However, I couldn’t escape Alex’s kabedon hold.

The answer was simple: the Level difference between Alex and me had not been overcome.

I put considerable force into resisting the restraint, but Alex didn’t budge. In fact, he deepened his smile, knowing I couldn’t escape. His expression had the ravenousness of a carnivore facing its prey.

“Alex!? Hey!! Wake up, Alex!!”

“…You’re not resisting…”

“I am! I am! I’m resisting with all my might!!”

“…Ah, I’ll let you pretend that’s the case…”

“It’s not an excuse!”

“…If this is a dream, don’t let me wake up…”

“It’s reality! So wake up!”

I stretched my back to escape Alex’s lips, which were closing in inch by inch.

The fact that I was taller than Alex was buying me time. But even that was only a momentary stall. Alex, who had placed his hands on my shoulders, put force into both to shorten my back. I fought back, and my entire body strained with creaking sounds.

“I can feel how much your heart is pounding because of me…”

“Of course, it is!? It is, isn’t it!?”

This pounding was not love or affection, though.

“…Don’t laugh. This is my first time… So, be gentle…”

“I can’t laugh!?”

I was the one being attacked, and yet I was the one who’s supposed to be taking him!?

This was beyond abnormal.

Where, and how, did he get such a troublesome fetish?

…Damn it, but his face was cute!

Alex’s expression, reaching its limit with anguish, was indeed that of a beautiful girl who made you want to attack her. If Alex were a girl, I would have embraced her, and if I were a girl, I would have embraced him. That’s the kind of destructive power he possessed. I found it strange that I could remain sane, even though it wouldn’t be surprising to misunderstand the situation.

Alex closed his eyes.

Holding his breath, his eyelashes trembling.

He slightly thrust his chin out, soliciting a kiss.

Despite my desperate resistance, the one-centimeter gap between Alex and me gradually narrowed. It’s no use. It’s over. I tightly closed my eyes and waited for the final moment… and felt something hot touch my lips.

“Nuh-uh.”

Surprised by the voice, I opened my eyes.

“Barely safe, right?”

It was Cindy.

She held several skewers of grilled meat, from which white steam was cheerfully rising, and one of them was inserted between Alex’s and my lips. The savory smell of well-cooked, marinated meat tickled my nostrils. Since a generous amount of spices were used as preservatives, the scent, not just the taste, was quite stimulating.

“—Ouch, that’s hot!? And spicy!?”

“Hot!? W-what’s going on… Ouch!?”

The heat of the skewer seemed to have finally brought Alex back to his senses.

He recoiled backward, tears in his eyes, clutching his lips that were throbbing in pain.

Finally released, I was genuinely relieved.

“Good, it looks like you’re back to the old Alex.”

“I’m back to the old me… Hah, no way… Was that just a dream…?”

Saying that, Alex’s face turned beet red, and he quickly covered his chest.

No, why would you do that? What kind of reaction was that for a guy?

“Ah, well, the pain and heat hadn’t completely subsided, I guess. That’s probably why you were a little confused… So, I’m forgetting what just happened.”

“Cindy didn’t see anything, either. Nothing.”

“Ugh! Kuuuh… Th-thank you… I’m sorry…!”

Alex covered his face with his hair and completely shut down.

I had nothing more to say to him.

“Alex. Eat this.”

“…Thank you, Cindy…”

“See ya. Borrowing Zaryū.”

I was a little worried about Alex, who was slumped on the ground in a duck sitting position, but I let Cindy lead me away.

“Zaryū is full of openings.”

“I’m ashamed.”

“Have you reflected?”

“Yes.”

I was thinking about the three people who had experienced an unusual change in their condition due to the ointment massage.

I could forcibly rationalize that Marī and Clair, well, since we had a physical relationship, it wasn’t strange that things developed in that direction, but I couldn’t figure out why Alex was being so seductive.

“Liar.”

So, I had responded to Cindy absent-mindedly.

By the time I realized the words that were reprimanding me, it was already too late.

“Moguh!?”

“Mmmh… Chu, chu… Kuchu… Pwah! That was a very spicy kiss, right?”

“Y-you!? What was that, suddenly!?”

“Punishment and reward.”

Cindy declared that it was a punishment for responding absent-mindedly and a reward for helping me with Alex’s situation. She stuck out her bright red tongue and licked the sauce off her lips. Was that the sauce that was on my lips?

“Zaryū is still full of openings.”

Cindy wore a mischievous smile.

I was completely outplayed.

“Hah, you’re absolutely right. Thanks to you, my head is clear.”

If I had been in my normal state, I wouldn’t have had my lips stolen so easily.

It was frustrating, but I couldn’t talk back. But…

“Why was it a kiss?”

“I heard about Zaryū. That you worked hard for Cindy.”

Uncharacteristically, she fidgeted a little and quietly let out,

“So, a thank you.”

“Hahaha, that’s a pretty lavish reward I got.”

“With this, Zaryū will be head-over-heels for Cindy.”

“That’s not happening.”

“Che!”

Cindy pouted dramatically when I denied it.

“Too bad. Cindy will eat mean Zaryū’s grilled meat skewer.”

“Hey! That’s not fair!?”

And so, a short game of tag began between Cindy and me.

The result was my complete defeat. I did get the grilled meat skewer, but I was a little frustrated when she said, “You owe me one,” but… well, I was relieved to see Cindy back to her usual energetic self.

Soon after, our rest period ended.

Together with the rejoined Bernkatze, we headed for the deepest part of the dungeon.

+++

# **81 - What Sleeps In The Heart Of Stillness (1)**

I brought Marī and the others back to the spot where I had found the clue.

Immediately, I had Marī decipher the letters that I couldn’t read. She traced the letters that were invisible to the naked eye with her finger through the lens of a Magic Tool, reading them one by one. Her fingertip stopped several times. She was likely flipping through the dictionary of her memory to extract the meaning contained within the words.

In this world, there are many races with physical and outward characteristics that fall outside the human—or perhaps Homo Sapiens—frame. In the slum where we lived, the number of such races we saw increased due to the influx of many refugees over the past few years due to the war. I felt the presence of races that we had previously only seen a few times a year during the traveling merchant season.

The famous races familiar from my previous life would be Dwarves and Elves. Cindy, a Halfling, looked like an innocent young girl but was older than me. The Dwarf man I had met once was shorter than Cindy but had a stout build, and with his magnificent beard, he clearly displayed the dignity of an elder. Surprisingly, he, who was far longer-lived than humans at 160 years old, said he was still young among Dwarves.

I had also encountered races with the characteristics of beasts, like dogs and cats, and in very rare cases, people with the appearance of bipedal lizards. Seeing people of vastly different appearances cross paths in town on a daily basis makes me feel that differences in skin or eye color are relatively minor… but the reality is not so. As the number of refugees settling in the slum increased year by year, the troubles arising from differences in race and culture also continued to increase.

Still, the only reason we managed to get by was that the language we used was the same, even if our races were different.

We could communicate with each other. Even if a person’s appearance was vastly different from my own, that alone offered some reassurance that the person was also human. If we couldn’t exchange words with each other, I believe the situation in the slum would have been much more cutthroat.

That’s probably why.

I felt a strong sense of incongruity that the unique language used in Marra was vastly different from the common language we spoke.

There were also words, subtle intonation differences, and unique habits in the common language that were only used among people of the same nation, culture, or race. It was rather natural for a language to have dialects.

The common language used phonetic characters, so people from other places could read and hear it, and even if the spelling was slightly wrong, if it was converted to sound, people from the same region could generally understand the meaning.

However, the language used in Marra did not conform to this.

The angularly designed characters were abstract, complex, and bizarre. They seemed to be ideograms.

In terms of the knowledge from my previous life, Kanji, Hieroglyphs, Mesopotamian cuneiform, and Pictograms would fit the description. Due to the nature of the script being deeply tied to the culture and history, only those born and raised in Marra or those who had studied Marra culture and language could decipher the writing.

A mysterious great nation that dared not use the common language spoken across the entire continent.

That was Marra, a nation culturally isolated.

I looked around.

Although this area was now called a dungeon, it seemed to have been a very ordinary passage connecting the underground of the city of Marra back then. Holograms supported by the Artificial Spirit were projected in my field of vision. Among them was one that guided people to an emergency evacuation shelter. This must be because they lived in a peaceful country and era. Seeing an unfamiliar word made me feel tense.

The long, orderly, straight passage.

I observed the various steps, stairs, and waterways throughout the area.

As I did so, I realized that my memories from my previous life were being stimulated somehow.

Nostalgic memories of being jostled on a crowded subway.

Days that flew by as I was relentlessly chased by a mountain of work.

Weekends disappeared as I only rested my body for the sake of work.

If I asked myself if I wanted to go back to those days… a vaguely ambiguous expression surfaced on my face.

It was then that I suddenly realized. I couldn’t recall the details of my previous life.

My memory felt significantly faded. I didn’t think I had a bad memory, but it was natural since more than a decade had passed since I was reincarnated here.

Perhaps I would eventually forget everything about my past life as if it were a dream.

That thought brought a bit of sadness… but, well, I didn’t need to indulge in sentimentality right now.

What I thought when looking at the Marra Dungeon was that Marra’s relics showed highly sophisticated systems in various places that reminded me of the megacities of my previous life. The nostalgia for my past life that I carried. I felt enough common resemblance and atmosphere between Marra and the streets of my past life to evoke that feeling.

It had been about an hour since we started the deciphering. The surroundings were quiet.

I had no intention of letting down my guard, but I was a little restless.

For a change of pace, I traced the destination of the insubstantial text projected in my vision.

I put my finger on the line extending from a part of the wall and pulled it up.

The cover opened easily, revealing a rotary lever inside.

A string of characters with annotations. It didn’t seem to be the kind of text that indicated danger.

Could this be the mechanism I was looking for to open the hidden passage?

“There’s a possibility.”

I moved the lever with a sound.

The sound of compressed air escaping.

The wall surface began to move, stirring up dust.

What appeared from inside was a metallic door.

It was heavy, with a handle in the center, much like a ship’s watertight door.

It was clear that the area beyond this point was strictly sealed.

“Wait! It’s dangerous to touch things on your own!”

I came back to my senses when I saw Marī’s angry face.

I had completely forgotten that she was in the middle of deciphering the text.

“Sorry!”

“If you could read it, there was no point in me working so hard to decipher it!”

“No, I just casually thought it might be okay… Sorry, I was spacing out.”

“Hah!? Are you an idiot!?”

“I’m really sorry!”

I quickly dropped to my knees, put all four limbs on the ground, and bowed my head.

The weight of my backpack and Marī’s piercing gaze pressed down heavily on me.

“It doesn’t matter, does it? It was the mechanism we were looking for, wasn’t it?”

“The monster we defeated earlier might be sealed in the depths again! Alex, use your head a little! Be aware that you’ve fallen into traps many times!”

“Guh…”

Alex’s fighting spirit was completely dampened by Marī’s icy glare.

“Senpai was spacing out because he’s not fully recovered yet—”

“If he’s not well, all the more reason to be careful. Clair, you haven’t forgotten that everyone almost died because you forced the teleporter to start, have you?”

“Y-yes…”

Clair, who tried to offer support, was instantly silenced by the intense, angry tone.

“Cindy, you’re the most observant, so you should have noticed Zarumen’s actions first.”

“Sorry, Marī.”

I heard Cindy’s voice drop as she slumped her shoulders.

It seemed she was genuinely dejected. She was recovering from an illness just like me.

I felt like I had done a bad thing.

“No, she was busy taking care of the surroundings and—”

“You can do that, too. Don’t just stand there staring at Alex’s butt, contribute to the Party with some work for once!”

“W-w-w-I wasn’t staring at the young master’s butt!? Furthermore, guarding the young master is my only mission!? And besides, my visor is fully down, so there’s no way you could know where I was looking!?”

Bernkatze frantically denied it.

His reaction was the very definition of guilty by protest.

Even Alex, hearing the exchange, instinctively covered his butt with his hand and distanced himself from Bernkatze. Bernkatze groaned and hung his head, losing all strength.

“…Haa, really, get a grip. I’m going to be in trouble if you don’t realize you’re the lifeline of this Party.”

Marī, muttering that, touched my forehead with her hand. It was slightly cool and comfortable.

Then, she grabbed my cheeks with both hands and peered into my eyes up close.

“You don’t seem to have a fever. You don’t seem to care much, but you almost died, so be more careful. Don’t push yourself for something like this.”

Something like this?

That’s not fair to say!

I swallowed the words that were about to leap out of my mouth.

“I’m fine. Thank you for worrying about me.”

I stood up and slapped my cheeks.

Thinking that another person’s life was more important than my own.

That feeling was the same for me as it was for Marī.

“Now I’m completely ready. Come on, let’s head inside and get the treasure!”

I acted with a deliberately cheerful tone.

Spacing out and indulging in nostalgia was truly foolish.

I should not dwell on the past but focus firmly on the present and the future.

The feeling of indignation at her words, which treated her own life lightly, was exactly the feeling she was directing toward me. I shouldn’t let her herself call the wish and purpose of saving her life “something like this.”

I turned to face the heavy door, like a watertight door, in front of me.

Beyond this point was a strictly protected area.

If the Magic Tool we were looking for was anywhere, it must be ahead.

“Marī, are we good to proceed beyond this point?”

I asked for confirmation.

“Yes, as far as I could decipher, there should be a residential area ahead. It seems it was prepared for citizens to live in as an evacuation facility in case of a disaster.”

“Understood. Then I’ll open it.”

I placed my hand on the handle and slowly turned it.

After feeling the lock disengage, I pulled the heavy iron door toward me to open it.

Someone behind me let out a small gasp of admiration.

Lights illuminated the passage that extended into the distance on its own.

“The walls and floor are white. And this texture doesn’t seem to be stone.”

Alex stepped onto the clean-looking corridor, tapping the floor with his foot and touching the wall as he commented.

“No sign of enemies. No traps. Probably safe.”

Cindy looked around and gave her assessment.

“There’s another door in the distance.”

The door Clair pointed to was not constructed like the bulkheads at the entrance.

Instead, it was wood-grained with some retro decorations. At the top was a design resembling a clock cut in half. Could it be? That thing. My heart fluttered at the unexpected sight.

“That’s a Lift.”

I was surprised by the answer that came from Marī’s mouth.

“Is that the Lift said to be in the Grand Cathedral of the Holy City?”

“I heard that it was a technology used in mines, but they have it inside a dungeon, too.”

“Cindy is seeing it for the first time. Excited.”

Clair, Alex, and Cindy also seemed to know about it from knowledge.

If I thought about it calmly, the Elevator was a technology that existed even before the common era in my past life.

It wouldn’t be strange for it to have been invented and used in this world as well.

However, I was strangely bothered by the exterior of the Lift resembling the retro elevators I had seen in movies and such. The handle-operated metal door earlier was the same. Just by coming past a single wall in the dungeon, I felt like I had stepped into a different world.

Even just the relics and streets of former Marra remaining on the surface hinted at a high standard of living and technological prowess. Furthermore, Marī said that they had been drawing up magic power from underground and utilizing that energy in various forms.

Judging by my knowledge, that was the concept of electricity itself.

I sensed a different scent than the nostalgia I felt earlier.

The smell of burned asphalt and concrete.

The mixed scent of car exhaust and the perfume worn by office ladies passing by.

The flashbacked memory momentarily made my eyes dizzy.

I had no memory of Marra’s streets.

I wasn’t born and raised in Marra.

And yet.

Why.

Were the memories of Marra and my past life resonating?

I had never had this experience before.

It felt like I was instantly traveling back and forth between the past and the present.

My figure, dressed as a weary Adventurer and walking through the underground passage, overlapped with the image of myself from that time, wearing a tie and walking through the office district.

“Bern, Zarumen. You two hurry up and get in.”

“A-ah.”

I suppressed my agitation, pretended to be calm, and got into the Lift.

When Marī operated the panel, it began to move silently.

My thoughts were stirred by the slight feeling of floating that enveloped my entire body.

A thing that existed where it shouldn’t.

What was that called?

“It’s like an Oopart.”

The quiet voice Bernkatze let out stabbed my ears.

“…What does that mean?”

“I said nothing. Just talking to myself.”

He turned his back to me, refusing to answer.

Adventurers had opportunities to see superior relics of the past.

Weapons and armor that performed better and were more valuable than those of the current era. Magic Tools like Sky Ships. These masterpieces, which appeared in the tall tales, legends, and epics of heroes sung by Bards and passed down among Adventurers, strongly captivated people’s hearts. In this world, where Gods and legends were close at hand, and many nations that flourished more than the current era existed, the concept of an “Out-of-Place Artifact” did not exist.

But Bernkatze clearly said Oopart just now.

A word I had never heard since I was born into this world until today.

Could Bernkatze be a fellow Isekai Reincarnator like me?

There was an example of me. It wouldn’t be strange for there to be other Reincarnators.

But if he was a Reincarnator, should we even reveal it to each other?

I still couldn’t trust Bernkatze, whose face I had never even seen.

Instead, a strong sense of distrust and anxiety welled up towards him. I glanced at the silent knight. What was he thinking under that steel armor, standing motionless with his arms crossed?

Contrary to my troubled heart, the Elevator silently descended toward its destination.

+++

# **82 - What Sleeps In The Heart Of Stillness (2)**

A bell rang. The Lift seemed to have reached its destination.

“Zaryū, let’s go.”

A cold sweat had formed on my palms. I took a small breath to compose myself.

Prompted by Cindy, I slowly stepped out of the Lift.

“I intended not to be surprised by anything, but this… is beyond even my imagination.”

Lush greenery. The sweet scent of flower nectar.

A rich fragrance that was detectable even by my nose, dulled by the smell of blood.

I felt a refreshing vitality and coolness.

“To think a place like this exists beneath a dungeon.”

The pleasant sound of a clear stream echoed in my ears.

It gently soothed my mind and body, which were fatigued from adventuring.

“It’s so beautiful. And the sunlight is warm… Is this really underground?”

The pouring sunlight made me mistake this for the surface.

A strong, dazzling light illuminated every corner of the beautiful garden equally.

A path paved with chalky white flagstones.

Benches and a gazebo seemed to be further along the path.

The Sanctuary I had seen in the dungeon before.

A scene that looked like a magnified version of that spread out before my eyes.

“Zaryū, look at that.”

“Are there living creatures here?”

My eyes met a family of deer peeking out from beyond the bushes.

If I listened closely, I could hear the chirping of birds, and if I looked closely at the flowers, butterflies were resting there.

The trees were laden with ripe, bell-like fruits.

Paradise.

That was my first impression of this place.

“…Could it be, something like this is the legacy boasted by the Magic City?”

Bernkatze threw a wet blanket over the emotion.

His words sounded as if they contained a small thorn.

Certainly, what we were looking for was a Magic Tool, not the ruins of a super-civilization.

In that regard, we were also left feeling disappointed.

However, his cold words seemed to contain a different intention.

“According to the story I heard from my father, the legend says, ‘Beyond the Paradise, the mystery and wisdom of Marra are sealed in the throne of the palace filled with light.’ I thought the garden we found before was it… but it seems this is the real one. That building over there must be the palace.”

I looked in the direction Alex pointed.

A chalky white spire subtly peeked out from beyond the green of the trees.

“Understood. Let’s aim for that tower first.”

I followed Alex’s words and proceeded at the front with Cindy.

Constructions like the flagstones, the fountain, and the waterways were beautiful, as if they had just been polished.

I could clearly see schools of fish swimming in the water.

“No dangerous feeling.”

“You’re right.”

A pastoral scene extended far into the distance.

I was distracted by the peaceful atmosphere, which was nothing like the desolate surface.

“There’s wheat growing over there. And potatoes. But no sign of people.”

There was no trace of human life anywhere.

Yet, only the environment necessary for people to live in was maintained.

“Why is that?”

“I have absolutely no idea.”

Cindy and I tilted our heads in unison.

“—Allow me to explain.”

I was startled by ADA’s voice abruptly cutting into the conversation.

Cindy didn’t seem to hear her voice. She was watching the movements of the adorable small animals while staying alert to the surroundings.

≪—This is the Chalk Globe. It is an underground garden constructed with a cyclical environmental model and a management system to maintain it. The spherical miniature garden is an oval shape with a high ceiling. If you imagine a chicken egg, the structure will be easy to understand. It is designed with consideration for the stress of living in a closed environment.≫

I looked up at the heavens in sync with ADA’s explanation.

The sky here was indeed high.

≪—It was built as an evacuation shelter assuming a World War or a Great Cataclysm. The maximum capacity is 100 people. It is constructed to withstand large-scale destruction at the level of the collapse of surface civilization.≫

Destruction at the level of the collapse of civilization.

Quite an alarming phrase came up.

What exactly was Marra fighting?

≪—Marra, located in the center of the continent, was a nation with much external pressure. War after war. The entire continent was stained with blood and fire. An era where no one knew the meaning of the word peace continued for a long time. The heroes who founded Marra sought every possible means to protect the momentary tranquility and peace they finally gained after pacifying the surrounding nations. As a result, the unparalleled development of Magic Technology arose and propelled Marra to become the largest nation on the continent. However, that simultaneously and inevitably stirred up the sense of crisis and hostility of the surrounding nations.≫

A sense of crisis toward a powerful neighbor, huh?

Moreover, Marra had a completely different culture from other nations.

A nation whose thoughts were unknown held the strongest power of anyone.

That might have appeared more terrifying than anything else in the eyes of the people at the time.

≪—And Marra incurred the wrath of Gods.≫

I remembered the God who brought me to this world.

≪—The fierce battle between the Manifested Gods and the founding heroes. It made the shining, glorious metropolis disappear from the face of the earth in a single night.≫

And the black monster we had just defeated.

I was told that was also a being called a God.

≪—The Gods burned down this nation, which was built with the wish for peace.≫

Their respective figures flickered in my mind.

The Artificial Spirit continued to speak dispassionately, showing no sign of concern for my agitation.

≪—It was all consumed, along with the prayers and wishes of over a million people.≫

The rustling of the trees blew through with an empty sound. The pouring sunlight and the blue of the sky felt strangely cold. The beautiful garden, which I had felt had the warmth and colors of life. That impression had now completely changed.

There was no sign of people in this garden where they should have been.

Nor were the people of Marra. Their prayers and wishes, either. So…

“ADA, answer me. We came here looking for an item that can undo a powerful curse, to save our comrade’s life. Placing our last hope on Marra’s superior Magic Tools… Hey, is our hope… still here?”

Was there only despair left for us?

I squeezed out the question I had intentionally avoided asking until now.

≪—Yes.≫

The answer that came back was clear and bright.

A single word infused with enough heat to melt my chilled mind and body.

≪—The Divine Elixir (Soma). A panacea that is said to remove all ailments and even resurrect the dead. A light curse that only erodes the flesh can be instantly un-cursed with just a spoonful.

“Is that true!?”

≪—Yes. There should be enough stored here to save the lives of the Marra citizens who evacuated during an emergency. There is no update to this information.≫

My whole body was trembling with joy.

She will be saved.

She will be saved.

Marī will be saved!

The wisdom, the legacy, the wish of Marra.

It had transcended time and connected as our hope.

“Zaryū is trembling. Are you okay?”

“Thank you, Cindy. I’ll be fine.”

Coming this far was the right choice.

Strength and heat surged into my steps and my tightly clenched fingertips.

“It doesn’t seem dangerous around here, so let’s pick up the pace a little.”

“Okay!”

I hurried ahead with Cindy.

My steps were light thanks to the flat ground and the flagstone path.

By simply increasing my stride a little, our marching speed increased significantly.

ADA was guiding me through the facilities and technology used in the garden near my ear.

The source of magic power, located even deeper underground than the underground dungeon, in the subterranean Paradise of the Chalk Globe. That seemed to be the energy source that supported the great city of Marra. Even now, a hundred years after the city’s destruction, the system for drawing up magic power continues to operate smoothly, powering various facilities and functions.

The technological prowess that created an artificially sustainable Paradise using magic power.

That was something not even achieved in my past life, where science was highly developed.

Such immense power that could manipulate everything in this world at will. Power like that of a God.

Did that drive not only the people of neighboring nations but also the hearts of the Gods who protected them to a madness of jealousy? Such legends remain in many religions, historical views, and narratives of my past life. They never forgive humans who get too close to the seat of God.

We were about to touch the secret treasure of Marra.

I could only pray that their anger would not turn toward us.

≪—We have reached the destination, so the voice guidance will now end.≫

I looked up at the magnificent gate towering before me.

It seemed to be made of the same chalky white building material as the palace.

The heavy doors opened on their own as we approached.

“Oh, a door that opens automatically when it senses a person.”

“Is there any possibility of a trap?”

“No, I don’t think so.”

Cindy and I exchanged glances and nodded.

“I agree with Cindy.”

“Then let’s explore inside quickly. We’re not here for sightseeing.”

Bernkatze urged us to proceed, saying that.

I stepped over the threshold of the palace with the utmost caution.

The sound of our shoes Katsun, Katsun, echoed in the high ceiling.

Beautiful chandeliers.

Intricate reliefs carved into the pillars and beams.

The exterior was simple, but the interior was gorgeous and splendid, preserving the wealth of Marra in its heyday. The corridor, lined with colorful carpets, wallpaper, landscape paintings, and pottery, was spectacular.

“W-what is this!?”

My eyes were drawn to the colossal crystal enshrined in the inner room.

A vertically long crystal, perhaps five meters tall, intricately cut. It floated in the air, radiating a rainbow glow. Metal rings and jewels orbited it like satellites, slowly rotating at a constant speed. It looked exactly like a Celestial Sphere. I could see many characters spelled out with magic power.

“So beautiful.”

“There probably isn’t such a magnificent Magic Tool even in the Royal Capital.”

I looked down at the floor and saw several black-discolored, shattered stones.

Did they fulfill their purpose? Or did they break… In any case, I assumed they were once floating around the crystal like the other jewels.

The area below the crystal consisted of tiered steps, like a circular stage. Perhaps people used to sit here and gaze at it instead of the night sky. I felt a strange sadness thinking that it had simply continued to mark time, silently, in the depths of this palace filled with stillness, in this place that everyone had forgotten, where there was no one to look up at it.

“Zaryū, look at that.”

I followed Cindy’s pointing finger.

There was a human silhouette in the center of the large crystal.

A woman sleeping with her hands clasped in front of her chest, as if in prayer. The crystal was glowing with a rainbow color, so I couldn’t tell the color of her skin or eyes. Her long, pointed ears and severely twisted horns were deeply impressive. It was the first time I had seen a race with characteristics like hers. Surely, a real human wasn’t trapped inside. I thought it was something like a marble sculpture in an art museum, but I felt a lifelike and alluring sensuality from her demeanor, as if she could come back to life at any moment.

A delicate yet beautiful face. Her eyes were open, but empty.

With a dreamlike expression, as if on the verge of slumber, she was staring at me.

I felt like she was trying to tell me something.

I was completely captivated by her. No, not just me. Marī, Clair, Cindy, and Alex were all captivated by the woman with the mystical aura, who stood solemnly within the crystal.

“We finally made it here.”

That’s why our reaction was a moment too slow.

A short sword pierced the crystal, tearing through the stillness.

Its blade was smeared with a pitch-black, filthy sludge.
